I detail what makes the divorced woman permissible. And marriage of a woman who is bā'in (irrevocably divorced) with less than three [divorces] is permissible in her iddah and after it. And a free woman is not permissible after three [divorces], nor a slave woman after two, until someone else has intercourse with her in a valid marriage, and [until] the iddah of his divorce or his death passes. His statement: 'and marriage' – it is either a conjunction to his statement 'and his intercourse with her', so then his statement 'in her iddah' is related to marriage, meaning the husband may marry a divorcée in the passive voice, i.e., the one divorced bā'in once or twice; or it is a subject whose predicate is his statement 'in her iddah', i.e., permissible or established in her iddah and after the iddah. His statement: 'in her iddah' – an objection is raised against it by His statement: 'And do not resolve on the marriage tie until the prescribed term reaches its end' (Quran 2:235), which indicates the prohibition of marriage during iddah absolutely, whether the one marrying is the first husband or another. And it is answered: that the husband is exempted from it by consensus, and others are prohibited from it to avoid confusion of lineage of children, and there is no confusion in the first husband's marriage, because it only occurs when there is mixing of sperm. His statement: 'and after it' – meaning without need for a different husband's tahlīl; and that is because legality does not disappear absolutely without three. This is indicated by His statement: 'And if he divorces her—that is, thrice—then she is not lawful to him afterward until she marries a husband other than him' (Quran 2:230), where the removal of legality is suspended on the third divorce. His statement: 'nor a slave woman after two' – because, as has passed, two divorces in the case of a slave woman are like three for a free woman, whether her husband is a slave or free; for, according to us, both divorce and iddah are determined by the woman. His statement: 'until he has intercourse with her' – by its generality he indicates that it is more general than being real (physical) and being legal (constructive), as when she marries a man whose penis is amputated and she becomes pregnant from him, and that ejaculation is not required, rather mere insertion; because ejaculation is the perfection of intercourse, and the text that indicates the requirement of intercourse does not indicate it. 'Other than him with a valid marriage, and the iddah of his divorce or his death passes': This is the view of the majority, and according to Sa'īd ibn al-Musayyab, intercourse of the second husband is not required, rather mere marriage suffices, citing His statement: 'until she marries a husband other than him.' (Quran 2:230). His statement: 'other than him' – even if he is an adolescent, or a eunuch, or impotent, or one whose penis is amputated, or a dhimmī for a dhimmī woman. So in 'Al-Bahr'. His statement: 'with a valid marriage' – so fornication does not suffice for tahlīl, nor intercourse in an invalid marriage, which is a marriage lacking a condition for its validity. His statement: 'this' – meaning the requirement of the second husband's intercourse in the chapter of tahlīl is the school of the majority of the four imams and their followers and others, so even if the second husband divorces before entry or dies before it, she is not lawful for the first. His statement: 'by His statement' – the summary: Allah made the limit of the prohibition of the thrice-divorced woman from the first husband the marriage of that woman to another husband, and He did not mention intercourse, so this indicates that it is not a condition. And the majority who require intercourse took two approaches: 1. Among them are those who chose that 'nikāh' in this verse means intercourse; how could it not be, for nikāh linguistically means union, and it is realized by intercourse, and it has been used in that sense in His statement: 'And test the orphans until they reach the age of marriage' (Quran 4:6). Thus, the Book indicates the requirement of intercourse. And it is supported by the fact that if nikāh meant contract, the word 'husband' in that verse would suffice, so...
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Wiqāyah clarifies the conditions under which a woman who has been divorced three times becomes permissible for her first husband. The author opens with the main ruling: a free woman after three divorces, and a slave woman after two, is not lawful for her previous husband until she marries another man, has intercourse with him in a valid marriage, and then completes her iddah either from his divorce or his death. The commentary then explains each part. The phrase 'marriage of a bā'in woman with less than three' means the first husband can remarry his wife during her iddah or after it if the divorce was bā'in but less than three (i.e., one or two). This is despite the general prohibition of marrying a woman during her iddah (Quran 2:235); the husband is exempted by consensus because there is no confusion of lineage—the child would be attributed to the husband even if the water is mixed. The phrase 'after it' means no need for tahlīl by another husband because the marriage bond is not completely severed until the third divorce, as indicated by Quran 2:230. For a slave woman, two divorces have the same effect as three for a free woman, whether her husband is free or slave, because according to the Hanafi school, both divorce and iddah are based on the woman's status. The word 'intercourse' (wat') includes both actual intercourse and constructive intercourse (e.g., pregnancy from a man with a severed penis), and it does not require ejaculation—mere insertion suffices because the texts that require wat' do not specify ejaculation. The passage then addresses a key dispute: the majority of scholars (including the four imams) require actual intercourse, while Sa'īd ibn al-Musayyab holds that mere marriage contract suffices, citing the literal meaning of 'nikāh' in Quran 2:230 as contract. The author explains that those who require intercourse interpret 'nikāh' in the verse as intercourse, as it is linguistically used for union and is attested in Quran 4:6. Alternatively, even if 'nikāh' is taken as contract, the requirement of intercourse is established by other evidence such as the hadith that 'she does not become lawful until she tastes the sweetness and bitterness of the second husband.' The second husband must be someone other than the first; he can be a minor, eunuch, impotent, or dhimmī, but the marriage must be valid—fornication or an invalid marriage does not count. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that of the majority: intercourse is necessary; mere contract is insufficient.

Key Terms
مبانة (mubānah): A woman divorced irrevocably (bā'in) with one or two divorces (less than three), so she is not lawful for the husband without a new marriage.
وطء (waṭʾ): Sexual intercourse; in this context, it includes both actual penetration and constructive intercourse (e.g., pregnancy from a man with a severed penis), but does not require ejaculation; mere insertion suffices.
نكاح صحيح (nikāḥ ṣaḥīḥ): A valid marriage contract meeting all conditions of legitimacy, as opposed to fornication or an invalid (fāsid) marriage.
عدة (ʿiddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of her husband before remarrying, here specifically the iddah after the second husband's divorce or death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in this passage, what is required for a free woman divorced three times to become halal for her first husband?
A) She must marry a second husband in a valid contract and complete her iddah, but consummation is not required.
B) She must marry a second husband, consummate the marriage, and complete the iddah from that marriage.
C) She can remarry the first husband immediately after a valid marriage contract with a second husband.
D) She must have intercourse with a second husband, but the marriage contract need not be valid.

Key Takeaway
A thrice-divorced woman becomes halal for her first husband only after a valid marriage, consummation, and completed iddah with another man.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Meaning of Nikah in Verse 2:230 and Condition of Intercourse
Linguistic and hadith-based proof that nikah means intercourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school interprets 'nikah' in Quran 2:230 as intercourse and evaluate the counter-argument based on linguistic attribution.

Core Idea
Interpreting 'nikah' as intercourse avoids repetition and is supported by explicit hadith requiring 'tasting the honey'.

This lesson dives into the linguistic and hadith-based arguments that shape the Hanafi position on the condition of intercourse for remarriage after a triple divorce. The passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah presents both the Hanafi proof and the objections, culminating in a clear preference for the requirement of actual intercourse. Understanding this debate is crucial for correctly applying the ruling in matters of marital law.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school holds regarding the meaning of 'nikah' in Quran 2:230 ('hatta tankiha'). The verse is about a woman who has been divorced three times; she is not halal for her first husband until she marries another man. The Hanafi position is that 'nikah' here means intercourse, not just the marriage contract.
This is based on the principle that interpreting it as intercourse adds a new condition (tasis), whereas interpreting it as contract would be mere repetition (takrar).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
An objection is raised: scholars who hold that 'nikah' means contract only. Their key proof is linguistic: the word 'nikah' is attributed to the woman in the verse ('tankiha'), but intercourse is not typically attributed to a woman (one does not say 'wati'ah' for a woman). Therefore, the verse must refer to the contract, which can be attributed to both parties.
This objection is typical of the Shafi'i school, though not exclusively.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response to the linguistic objection
The Hanafi response argues that attributing intercourse to a woman is linguistically possible, as seen in the word 'zaniyah' (adulteress), which derives from 'zina' (unlawful intercourse). Though 'wati'ah' is not common, the lack of common usage does not make it impossible. Thus, the attribution of 'nikah' to the woman does not force it to mean contract.
This response shows that the linguistic objection is not decisive.
4
Consider the metaphorical interpretation and the second approach
Some Hanafi scholars concede that 'nikah' literally means contract but is used metaphorically in this verse for 'allowing intercourse' due to the context of hadith. A second approach holds that 'nikah' means contract only, and the condition of intercourse is derived separately from hadith. This second approach also allows jurists to deduce that a woman can contract her own marriage, a point of disagreement with al-Shafi'i.
The commentator notes that the disagreement with al-Shafi'i on women contracting marriage is mentioned elsewhere.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference is clear: if 'nikah' means contract, then a valid marriage contract alone (even without consummation) would make the woman halal for the first husband. If it means intercourse, then actual sexual intercourse is required. The Hanafi position, supported by multiple hadith, insists on actual intercourse.
The hadith evidence (e.g., 'not until you taste his honey') is strong and decisive for the Hanafi school.

طلاقاً بائناً ، فتزوجت بعده عبد الرحمن بن الزبير القرظي فطلقها، فأتت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إنه طلقني قبل أن يمسني ، أفأرجع إلى الأوّل، فقال: لا، حتى يمس»، فلبثت فقالت : حتى قبض النبي فأتت أبا بكر فقالت : أرجع إلى الأوّل، فإنّ الآخر قد مسني، فقال أبو بكر : عهدت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال لك ما قال لا ترجعي إليه ، فلما مات أبو بكر أتت إلى عمر ، فقال لها : لإن أتيتني بعد هذه المرة لأرجمنك».
وأخرج الشافعي وأحمد وعبد الرزاق وابن أبي شيبة والبخاري ومسلم والترمذي والنسائي وابن ماجة والبيهقي عن عائشة رضي الله عنها: «جاءت امرأة رفاعة القرظي إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقالت : إني كنت عند رفاعة فبت طلاقي، فتزوجني عبد الرحمن بن الزبير، وما معه إلا مثل هدبة الثوب ، فتبسم النبي الله ، فقال : أتريدين أن ترجعي إلى رفاعة، لا حتى تذوقي عسيلته ويذوق هو عسيلتك».
وأخرج البخاري ومسلم والنسائي وابن جرير والبيهقي عن عائشة رضي الله عنها: «إنّ رجلاً طلق امرأة ثلاثاً فتزوجت زوجاً وطلّقها قبل أن يمسها، فسئل النبي : أتحل للأول ، قال : «لا حتى يذوق من عسيلتها كما ذاق الأول»(٢).
(۲)
وأخرج مالك والشافعي وابن سعد والبيهقي عن الزبير بن عبد الرحمن بن الزبير: «إنّ رفاعة ابن سموال القرظي طلق امرأته تميمة بنت وهب في عهد رسول الله ثلاثاً فنكحها عبد الرحمن بن الزبير، فاعترض عنها فلم يستطع أن يمسها ففارقها ، فأراد رفاعة أن ينكحها، وهو زوجها الأول، فذكر ذلك لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال رسول الله لا تحل لك حتى تذوق العسيلة»(۳).
:
(٤)
وفي الباب روايات أخر مبسوطة في «الدر المنثور للسيوطي، وستطلع ما يرد
على هذا المسلك.
If the word 'nikah' in His statement 'until she marries' is interpreted as merely the contract, then repetition would be necessary. But if it is interpreted as intercourse, then it becomes an original statement, and originality is preferable to emphasis and repetition. An objection was raised against them: that intercourse is not attributed to the woman as an act, so one does not say 'a woman who commits intercourse' (wati'ah); rather, one says 'the man is the one who commits intercourse' (al-wati'), and 'she is the one with whom intercourse is done' (al-mawtuyyah). As for the contract, it is attributed to both. Since 'nikah' in the verse is attributed to the woman, that indicates that what is meant is the contract, not intercourse. The answer is: there is no impossibility in attributing intercourse to her; hence she is called 'zaniyah' (adulteress), even though it is clear that zina is unlawful intercourse. The only point is that the term 'wati'ah' is not commonly used for her. 2. Some of them said: even if nikah is a reality in contract, here it is taken metaphorically as her allowing intercourse, due to the context of many hadith and reports indicating the condition of intercourse. The second approach: that what is meant by nikah in the verse is the contract only, and on this basis the jurists deduced the validity of a woman contracting her own marriage. In this there is a disagreement with al-Shafi'i, because in his view marriage is not valid by the woman's own statement, and this has been mentioned in its place. As for the condition of intercourse, it is from the hadith that have been transmitted indicating that, and they are many and famous. Ahmad and al-Nasa'i narrated from 'Ubayd Allah ibn 'Abbas: that al-Ghumaysa' or al-Rumaysa' came to the Prophet complaining that her husband did not have intercourse with her, and before long her husband came and said: 'O Messenger of Allah, she is lying; he does have intercourse with her, but she wants to return to her first husband.' So the Messenger of Allah said: 'That is not for you until another man tastes your honey.' And Ibn al-Mundhir narrated from Muqatil that he said: this verse was revealed concerning 'A'ishah bint 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Atik al-Nasri; she was married to Rifa'ah ibn Wahb ibn 'Atik, who was her cousin, and he divorced her with a final divorce. Then she married 'Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Zubayr al-Qurazi, and he divorced her. So she came to the Prophet and said: 'He divorced me before touching me; may I return to the first?' He said: 'No, until he has intercourse.' She waited until the Prophet passed away, then she came to Abu Bakr and said: 'May I return to the first, for the other has touched me?' Abu Bakr said: 'I heard the Prophet say to you what he said: do not return to him.' When Abu Bakr died, she came to 'Umar, and he said: 'If you come to me after this again, I will stone you.' And al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, 'Abd al-Razzaq, Ibn Abi Shaybah, al-Bukhari, Muslim, al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i, Ibn Majah, and al-Bayhaqi narrated from 'A'ishah: 'The wife of Rifa'a al-Qurazi came to the Messenger of Allah and said: I was with Rifa'a and he divorced me finally. Then I married 'Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Zubayr, and he has nothing like the fringe of a garment.' The Prophet smiled and said: 'Do you want to return to Rifa'a? No, until you taste his honey and he tastes your honey.' And al-Bukhari, Muslim, al-Nasa'i, Ibn Jarir, and al-Bayhaqi narrated from 'A'ishah: that a man divorced his wife three times, and she married another husband who divorced her before touching her. So the Prophet was asked: 'Is she permissible for the first?' He said: 'No, until he tastes from her honey as the first tasted.' And Malik, al-Shafi'i, Ibn Sa'd, and al-Bayhaqi narrated from al-Zubayr ibn 'Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Zubayr: that Rifa'a ibn Simwal al-Qurazi divorced his wife Tamimah bint Wahb three times in the time of the Prophet. Then 'Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Zubayr married her, but he turned away from her and could not touch her, so he separated from her. Rifa'a wanted to marry her again, and he was her first husband. He mentioned that to the Messenger of Allah, and the Messenger of Allah said: 'She is not permissible for you until you taste the honey.' There are other narrations on this topic, detailed in al-Suyuti's 'al-Durr al-Manthur', and you will see what is objected to this approach.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah on Sharh al-Wiqayah, addressing the meaning of 'nikah' in Quran 2:230. It begins by presenting the linguistic argument: if 'nikah' meant merely the marriage contract, the verse would be repetitive (since the condition of remarrying after divorce is already implied). But if it means intercourse, it adds a new condition, which is preferable in interpretation. The commentator then reports an objection: that 'intercourse' is not attributed to a woman actively (one does not say 'she is a wati'ah'), whereas 'nikah' in the verse is attributed to the woman ('hatta tankiha'). The response is that there is no linguistic barrier, as 'zina' (unlawful intercourse) is attributed to a woman when she is called 'zaniyah', even though it is an act of unlawful intercourse. The lack of common usage of 'wati'ah' does not negate the possibility. Then a second view is mentioned: that 'nikah' is transferred metaphorically to mean 'allowing intercourse' due to the context of the hadith. The commentator then clarifies the second approach: some hold that 'nikah' means only the contract, from which jurists deduced that a woman can contract her own marriage. Here al-Shafi'i differs, holding that a woman cannot be the contracting party. However, the main point is the condition of intercourse, which is established by numerous hadith. The passage then lists several narrations: the hadith of al-Ghumaysa'/al-Rumaysa', the story of 'A'ishah bint 'Abd al-Rahman, the hadith of the wife of Rifa'a, the hadith of the man who divorced thrice, and the narration of al-Zubayr. All emphasize that the woman is not halal for the first husband until the second husband has actually had intercourse with her. The commentator notes that there are further narrations in al-Suyuti's al-Durr al-Manthur. The discussion reinforces the Hanafi position that 'nikah' in this verse means intercourse, and the condition is proven by prophetic hadith.

Key Terms
النكاح (al-nikah): In this passage, debated whether it means marriage contract or sexual intercourse in the context of Quran 2:230.
الوطء (al-wat'): Sexual intercourse; the condition for a divorced woman to remarry her first husband after an intervening marriage.
العسيلة (al-'usaylah): Metaphor for honey or sweetness of intercourse; used in hadith to denote sexual intimacy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi interpretation of Quran 2:230, what does 'hatta tankiha' mean in the context of a woman remarrying her first husband after a triple divorce?
A) Until she enters into a marriage contract with another man
B) Until she has sexual intercourse with another man
C) Until she receives a dowry from another man
D) Until she completes the waiting period with another man

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires actual intercourse with the second husband, proven by hadith, before a triple-divorced woman can remarry her first husband.

Hadith of al-Usaylah: Proof for Consummation in Tahleel
Defending the requirement of consummation for tahleel via hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the minimum requirement for consummation in tahleel and explain how the hadith of al-Usaylah serves as proof, including the usul principle of specification (takhsees) by a mashhur hadith.

Core Idea
Mere penetration suffices for tahleel; the diminutive 'usaylah' indicates minimal contact, not climax.

This lesson examines the Hanafi school's reliance on the well-known hadith of al-Usaylah to require consummation in a second marriage for a triple-divorced woman to become lawful to her first husband. The hadith's metaphor of 'tasting honey' is analyzed linguistically to determine the minimum act required, and an important usul objection regarding the use of an ahad hadith to add a condition to the Quran is addressed through the concept of specification (takhsees).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its primary proof
The Hanafi ruling is that a triple-divorced woman must consummate a valid second marriage to be lawful for her first husband. The primary proof is the hadith of al-Usaylah: 'No, until you taste his 'usaylah and he tastes your 'usaylah.'
2
Analyze the linguistic derivation from the diminutive
The word 'usaylah is the diminutive of 'asl (honey). The diminutive form indicates minimal involvement. Hanafi scholars derive that mere insertion (penetration) suffices, and ejaculation or full pleasure is not required.
Contrast with the requirement for the marriage itself, which must be complete and valid.
3
Address the usul objection: adding to the Quran with ahad hadith
The objection is that ahad hadith cannot add a condition not found in the Quran (which only mentions marriage). The Hanafi response: this hadith is mashhur (well-known), not ordinary ahad, and it specifies (takhsees) the general command of marriage, which is permissible in the Hanafi school.
Hanafis distinguish between abrogation (naskh) and specification (takhsees).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab differences
All Hanafi imams agree on the requirement of consummation, but Abu Hanifa holds that mere penetration suffices, while the Sahibayn are silent on the degree. Other schools like the Shafi'is also require consummation but some may require ejaculation.
The mufta bihi is penetration suffices.
5
Apply the ruling: what if the second marriage is void or the intercourse is prohibited?
From the absolute wording of the hadith, the commentator derives that even if intercourse occurs in a prohibited context (e.g., fasting, menstruation), it still fulfills the condition of tahleel, though the man sins.
The condition is the biological act, not the legal permissibility of the act.

ولنا : حديث العسيلة 
وهو حديث مشهور ، تجوز الزيادة به على الكتاب 
[١] قوله : حديث العسيلة ؛ هو بالضمّ تصغير العسل، بالفارسية: شهد؛ أي الحجة لنا الحديث الذي ورد فيه ذكرُ العسيلة، وهو قوله  لامرأة رفاعة : «لا حتى تذوقي عسيلته ويذوق هو عسيلتك»، وهو كناية عن لذة الجماع، واستنبطوا من صيغة التصغير أنه لا يشترط في الوطء الإنزال، وكماله بل مجرد الإيلاج، فإنّ بالإنزال يتم فعل الوطء، وتكمل اللذة. فإن قلت : فما بالهم اشترطوا في النكاح الثاني المحلّل كونه كاملاً صحيحاً، حتى لو نكحت نكاحاً فاسدا لم تحل للأوّل ، ولم يشترطوا في الوطء كماله. قلت : لأن النكاح منصوص في الكتاب بقوله: ﴿ حَتَّى تَنكِحَ زَوْجًا غَيْره ) ، فيحل بإطلاقه على الفرد الكامل المعتبر شرعاً ، وهو النكاح المستجمع لجميع شروطه. وأمّا الوطء فمذكور في الحديث بلفظ التصغير، وهو يشعر بعدم اشتراط الكمال فيه، واستنبطوا أيضاً بإطلاق ذوق العُسيلة : أنّ المحلّل هو وطء الزوج الثاني مطلقاً وإن كان محرَّماً كالوطء حالة الصوم وحالة الحيض ونحو ذلك، فإنّ مثل هذا الوطء أيضاً يكون محللاً وإن أثم بفعله. [٢]قوله : وهو ... الخ ؛ دفع لما يَرِدُ على أصحاب المسلك الثاني الذين حملوا النكاح في الآية على مجرّد العقد، وأثبتوا اشتراط الوطء بالحديث، وهم فرقتان : فرقة تجوز الزيادة على الكتاب بأخبار الآحاد ، ونسخ إطلاقه بها كالشافعية، فلا إيراد عليهم. وفرقة تمنع الزيادة على الكتاب بأخبار الآحاد ونسخه بها كالحنفية كما مر تفصيله في شرح بحث الوضوء من «كتاب الطهارة». فيرد عليهم أن الحديث المثبت لاشتراط الوطء، وإن كان ثابتاً بأسانيد صحيحة لكنّه من أخبار الآحاد ، فكيف جوزتم به الزيادة على الكتاب فيما ورد به الكتاب، فإنّ الكتاب يحكم بكفاية النكاح وأنتم تشترطون معه الوطء أيضاً للتحليل.
And we have the hadith of al-Usaylah. And it is a well-known hadith; it is permissible to add to the Book by it. [The commentator says]: The saying: 'the hadith of al-Usaylah'; it is with a damma, the diminutive of 'asl (honey), in Persian: shahd; meaning our proof is the hadith in which 'usaylah is mentioned, and it is his saying to the wife of Rifa'a: 'No, until you taste his 'usaylah and he tastes your 'usaylah,' and it is a metaphor for the pleasure of intercourse. And they derived from the form of the diminutive that in sexual intercourse, ejaculation and its completion are not required, rather mere insertion, because through ejaculation the act of intercourse is completed and pleasure is perfected. If you say: Why then did they require the second marriage to be complete and valid, such that if she married with a void marriage she would not be lawful for the first husband, but they did not require completion in intercourse? I say: Because marriage is explicitly mentioned in the Book in His saying 'until she marries another husband,' so it applies by its absoluteness to the individual that is complete and considered valid in the law, which is the marriage that encompasses all its conditions. As for intercourse, it is mentioned in the hadith with the form of the diminutive, which indicates that completion is not required in it. And they also derived from the absolute wording of tasting the 'usaylah that the tahlil is the sexual intercourse of the second husband absolutely, even if it is prohibited like intercourse during fasting or menstruation and the like, for such intercourse also is a tahlil even though he sins by doing it. [The commentator says]: His saying 'and it is... etc.' is a rebuttal to what the proponents of the second approach (who interpreted marriage in the verse as merely the contract and established the condition of intercourse by the hadith) face. They are two groups: one group permits addition to the Book by ahad hadith and abrogation of its absolute meaning by them, like the Shafi'is, so there is no objection against them. And a group prohibits addition to the Book by ahad hadith and its abrogation by them, like the Hanafis, as detailed previously in the commentary on the discussion of wudu in the Book of Tahara. So an objection is raised against them: the hadith that establishes the condition of intercourse, although it is established through authentic chains, is from ahad hadith; how then did you permit addition to the Book by it in what the Book has stipulated? For the Book rules that marriage is sufficient, yet you stipulate intercourse with it for tahlil.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof: the Hanafi position that a woman divorced three times requires consummation in a second marriage to be lawful for her first husband. The proof is the well-known hadith of al-Usaylah, reported by multiple Companions, in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) told the wife of Rifa'a that she cannot return to Rifa'a until she tastes honey (al-Usaylah) from the second husband and he tastes from her. The Hanafi commentators derive from the diminutive form 'usaylah (small honey) that mere penetration suffices; ejaculation and full pleasure are not conditions. This contrasts with the marriage itself, which must be valid per the Quran's requirement. The commentator then addresses an important usul al-fiqh objection: Hanafis generally do not allow adding to the Quran by ahad hadith, yet here they use an ahad hadith to add the condition of intercourse. The response is twofold: First, the hadith is mashhur (well-known), which in the Hanafi view has a status between ahad and mutawatir and can specify ('iyadah) the Quran. Second, the Hanafis who prohibit addition (ziyada) in the sense of abrogation (naskh) treat this as a specification (takhsees), not an abrogation, and such specification by a mashhur hadith is permitted. Thus, the objection is rebutted.

Key Terms
عسيلة ('usaylah): Diminutive of 'asl (honey); metaphor for the pleasure of intercourse; used in the hadith to denote sexual intercourse.
زيادة على الكتاب (ziyada 'ala al-kitab): Addition to the Quranic text, i.e., introducing a condition or ruling not explicitly in the Quran.
حديث مشهور (hadith mashhur): A hadith transmitted by at least three companions in each generation; between ahad and mutawatir in strength.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Ejaculation is required.
B) Mere penetration (insertion) is sufficient.
C) Both partners must orgasm.
D) No intercourse is needed, only a valid marriage.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires consummation (penetration) in a valid second marriage for tahleel, derived from the mashhur hadith of al-Usaylah, and the diminutive indicates that minimal contact is sufficient.

Hanafi Defense for Requiring Intercourse in Tahlil Using Hadith al-Usaylah
Hanafi response to Shafi'i objection that ahad hadith cannot add to Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school requires intercourse for tahlil and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using usul principles.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school requires intercourse for tahlil, defended by companion consensus or the mashhur status of the hadith.

This lesson explores the inter-madhhab dispute on tahlil: Is intercourse required in the second marriage for a thrice-divorced woman to become lawful to her first husband? The Hanafi school insists it is, based on the hadith of al-'usaylah, while the Shafi'i school holds that mere marriage suffices, citing the Quranic verse. The core usul objection is that a hadith, if ahad, cannot add to the Quran. We examine two Hanafi defenses.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on tahlil
The Hanafi madhhab requires that the second husband have sexual intercourse with the woman for tahlil to be effective. Mere marriage contract is insufficient.
This is agreed upon by all three Hanafi imams.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection and its basis
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the Quranic verse (2:230) only mentions marriage (nikah), not intercourse, and that ahad hadith cannot add to the Quran.
The Shafi'i school permits addition by ahad hadith, but they reject this particular addition because they interpret the hadith differently.
3
Understand the usul objection specific to Hanafis
Hanafi usul prohibits adding to the Quran with ahad hadith. Critics argue that the hadith of al-'usaylah is ahad, so using it to require intercourse contradicts Hanafi principles.
This objection applies only to Hanafis; Shafi'is have no such internal conflict.
4
Examine the two Hanafi defenses
First defense: The hadith is supported by ijma' of the Companions, elevating it beyond ahad. Second defense (from al-Hidayah): The hadith is mashhur (well-known), which Hanafi usul permits for addition.
The second defense is criticized because the hadith is not technically mashhur; its fame is linguistic, not technical.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
Practically, if a judge rules that tahlil is valid without intercourse, the Hanafi position declares his ruling unenforceable because it contradicts established evidence.
The judgment may be excused for the judge's ijtihad, but it is not implemented.

ولنا : حديث العسيلة "، وهو حديث مشهور ، تجوز الزيادة به على الكتاب
[١] قوله : حديث العسيلة ؛ هو بالضمّ تصغير العسل، بالفارسية: شهد؛ أي الحجة لنا الحديث الذي ورد فيه ذكرُ العسيلة، وهو قوله ل ل لامرأة رفاعة : «لا حتى تذوقي عسيلته ويذوق هو عسيلتك»، وهو كناية عن لذة الجماع، واستنبطوا من صيغة التصغير أنه لا يشترط في الوطء الإنزال، وكماله بل مجرد الإيلاج، فإنّ بالإنزال يتم فعل الوطء، وتكمل اللذة. فإن قلت : فما بالهم اشترطوا في النكاح الثاني المحلّل كونه كاملاً صحيحاً، حتى لو نكحت نكاحاً فاسدا لم تحل للأوّل ، ولم يشترطوا في الوطء كماله. قلت : لأن النكاح منصوص في الكتاب بقوله: ﴿ حَتَّى تَنكِحَ زَوْجًا غَيْره ) ، فيحل بإطلاقه على الفرد الكامل المعتبر شرعاً ، وهو النكاح المستجمع لجميع شروطه. وأمّا الوطء فمذكور في الحديث بلفظ التصغير، وهو يشعر بعدم اشتراط الكمال فيه، واستنبطوا أيضاً بإطلاق ذوق العُسيلة : أنّ المحلّل هو وطء الزوج الثاني مطلقاً وإن كان محرَّماً كالوطء حالة الصوم وحالة الحيض ونحو ذلك، فإنّ مثل هذا الوطء أيضاً يكون محللاً وإن أثم بفعله. [٢]قوله : وهو ... الخ ؛ دفع لما يَرِدُ على أصحاب المسلك الثاني الذين حملوا النكاح في الآية على مجرّد العقد، وأثبتوا اشتراط الوطء بالحديث، وهم فرقتان : فرقة تجوز الزيادة على الكتاب بأخبار الآحاد ، ونسخ إطلاقه بها كالشافعية، فلا إيراد عليهم. وفرقة تمنع الزيادة على الكتاب بأخبار الآحاد ونسخه بها كالحنفية كما مر تفصيله في شرح بحث الوضوء من «كتاب الطهارة». فيرد عليهم أن الحديث المثبت لاشتراط الوطء، وإن كان ثابتاً بأسانيد صحيحة لكنّه من أخبار الآحاد ، فكيف جوزتم به الزيادة على الكتاب فيما ورد به الكتاب، فإنّ الكتاب يحكم بكفاية النكاح وأنتم تشترطون معه الوطء أيضاً للتحليل.
فيكون التحليل بدون الوطءِ مخالفاً للحديث المشهور، حتّى لو قضى القاضي به لا ينفذ.
وأجابوا عنه بوجهين :
الوجه الأول : : وهو أولاهما : إنّ هذا الحديث تأيد بالإجماع، فإنّ الصحابة أجمعوا على اشتراط الوطء، وقد ثبت هذا نصاً عن ابن مسعود وأنس وأبي هريرة وعلي وغيرهم على ما أخرجه ابن أبي شيبة في مصنفه»، ولم يعلم له مخالف في ذلك الصدر، فتصح الزيادة به على الكتاب.
فإن قلت: لو تحقق الإجماع لم يخالفه سعيد بن المسيب وهو من كبار التابعين الآخذين عن كبار الصحابة . قلت : لعله لم يصل إليه خبر هذا الإجماع ولم يصل إليه حديث العسيلة، وإلا لم يخالف، ولا بعد في أنّ لا يصل خبر بعض الجزئيات إلى بعض الأكابر ففوق كل ذي علم عليم، ومن علم حجّة على من لم يعلم عند كل ذي عقل سليم.
الوجه الثاني : ما اختاره صاحب «الهداية» وتبعه الشارح وغيره : إن حديث العسيلة من الأخبار المشهورة، والخبر المشهور تجوز به الزيادة على الكتاب، كما تقرر في علم الأصول، وأورد عليه أنه كونه مشهوراً بالمعنى اللغوي مسلّم. وأما بالمعنى الاصطلاحي الذي تجوز به الزيادة فممنوع، بل الصحيح أنه مع شهرته من أخبار الآحاد لم يصل إلى درجة التواتر ولا إلى درجة الشهرة، إلا أن يقال : هذا الحديث لما تلقته الأمة بالقبول فالمخالف فيه شاذ لم يعتد بـه ، صار في حكم المشهور، ولا يخفى ،وهنه، فإنّ تلقي الأمة بقبول حديث والعمل على وفقه لا يخرجه من حيز أخبار الآحاد ، ولا يدخله في المشهور الاصطلاحي
[١] قوله : لو قضى القاضي به ؛ أي بالتحليل بدون الوطء، ووجه عدم نفاذ القضاء فيه أنه مخالف لما دلّت عليه السنّة وأجمع عليه جمهور الأمة، بل نطقت به إشارة الآية، ومن شدّ فيه شدّ عن طريق سلف الأمة، وهو وإن كان معذوراً في حكمه باجتهاده، فالقاضي لا يكون معذوراً في القضاء، والمفتي في الإفتاء بـه بعـد وضوح الدلائل وسطوع الوسائل.
And our proof is the hadith of the honey, and it is a well-known hadith, by which addition to the Book is permitted. Meaning of the hadith of the honey: it is with a damma (on the 'ayn) a diminutive of honey, in Persian: shahd; i.e., our proof is the hadith in which the mention of honey occurs, and it is his statement to the wife of Rifa'a: 'No, until you taste his honey (sweetness) and he tastes your honey,' which is a metaphor for the pleasure of intercourse. And they deduced from the diminutive form that neither the discharge of semen nor completeness is required in intercourse, but mere insertion, because by discharge the act of intercourse is completed and pleasure is perfected. If you say: Why did they require in the second marriage (the tahlil marriage) that it be complete and valid, such that if she marries in a void marriage she does not become lawful for the first, but they did not require completeness in the intercourse? I say: Because marriage is mentioned in the Book by His statement: 'until she marries another husband' (2:230), so it is interpreted according to its absolute meaning as the complete individual considered legally, that is, the marriage that gathers all its conditions. As for intercourse, it is mentioned in the hadith in the diminutive form, which indicates the lack of requirement of completeness in it. And they also deduced from the absolute (expression) of tasting the honey that the tahlil is the intercourse of the second husband absolutely, even if it is forbidden like intercourse during fasting or menstruation and the like, for such intercourse also is tahlil even if he sins by his act. His statement: 'and it is...' etc.: a repelling of what might be objected to the followers of the second approach who interpreted marriage in the verse as mere contract and affirmed the condition of intercourse by the hadith. They are two groups: a group that permits addition to the Book by solitary reports and abrogation of its absolute (meaning) by them, like the Shafi'is, so no objection is upon them. And a group that prohibits addition to the Book by solitary reports and its abrogation by them, like the Hanafis, as its detail has passed in the commentary on the chapter of wudu from the Book of Purity. So it is objected to them: The hadith that establishes the condition of intercourse, even if it is established by authentic chains, is nevertheless among solitary reports, so how did you permit by it addition to the Book regarding what has come in the Book? For the Book rules the sufficiency of marriage while you require intercourse along with it for tahlil. Thus tahlil without intercourse contradicts the well-known hadith, such that if the judge judges by it, it is not executed. And they answered it in two ways: The first way: it is the better of the two that this hadith is supported by consensus, for the Companions agreed on the condition of intercourse. This has been established textually from Ibn Mas'ud, Anas, Abu Hurayra, 'Ali and others as reported by Ibn Abi Shayba in his Musannaf, and no opponent is known to them in that early period, so addition by it to the Book is valid. If you say: If consensus were established, Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib would not have opposed it, and he is among the great Followers (tabi'un) who took from the great Companions. I say: Perhaps the news of this consensus did not reach him, nor did the hadith of honey reach him; otherwise he would not have opposed. And there is no improbability that news of some particulars does not reach some great persons, for above every possessor of knowledge is one more knowledgeable, and knowledge is proof against the ignorant in the view of every sound intellect. The second way: what the author of al-Hidaya chose and followed by the commentator and others: that the hadith of honey is among the well-known (mashhur) reports, and the well-known report permits addition to the Book, as established in Usul al-Fiqh. But it is objected to it that it being well-known in the linguistic sense is conceded. As for the technical sense that permits addition, it is denied. Rather the correct view is that despite its fame it is among solitary reports, not reaching the degree of tawatur nor the degree of (technical) mashhur. Unless it is said: This hadith, since the ummah has received it with acceptance, the opponent to it is anomalous, not considered, so it becomes in the ruling of mashhur. But its weakness is not hidden, for the reception of the ummah of a hadith with acceptance and acting upon it does not take it out of the category of solitary reports and does not enter it into the technical mashhur. His statement: 'if the judge judges by it' i.e., by tahlil without intercourse, and the reason for its non-execution is that it contradicts what is indicated by the Sunnah and agreed upon by the majority of the ummah, rather the indication of the verse speaks of it, and whoever diverges in it has departed from the path of the predecessors (salaf) of the ummah. And even if he is excused in his ruling by his ijtihad, the judge is not excused in his judgment, nor the mufti in issuing a fatwa with it after the evidences are clear and the means are bright.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute defending the Hanafi requirement of intercourse in tahlil against the objection that ahad hadith cannot add to the Quran. The commentator (the author of Umdat al-Ri'ayah) begins by presenting the Hanafi proof: the hadith of al-'usaylah (the honey hadith), which is well-known and permits addition to the Book. He explains that the hadith refers to the wife of Rifa'a and uses a diminutive form ('usaylah, little honey) as a metaphor for intercourse. From this diminutive, Hanafi scholars deduce that full intercourse (including discharge) is not required; mere insertion suffices. The commentator then addresses a potential objection: Why is tahlil marriage required to be valid, while intercourse is not required to be complete? He answers by distinguishing between the Quranic text on marriage, which is absolute and requires a complete valid contract, and the hadith on intercourse, which is in a diminutive form indicating incompleteness. Furthermore, even if the intercourse is sinful (e.g., during fasting or menstruation), it still effects tahlil. The passage then focuses on the core dispute: Hanafis do not allow addition to the Quran by ahad hadith, yet they use this ahad hadith to require intercourse, which is an addition to the Quranic ruling that only marriage is needed. The commentator clarifies that there are two Hanafi defenses. The first defense: the hadith is supported by ijma' (consensus) of the Companions, making it acceptable to add to the Quran. He notes that the only reported opponent among the Tabi'un, Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib, likely did not receive the consensus or the hadith itself. The second defense, chosen by the author of al-Hidayah, is that the hadith is mashhur (well-known) in the technical sense, which Hanafi usul allows to add to the Quran. However, this is criticized: the hadith is only linguistically famous, not technically mashhur. The commentator concludes by noting that a judge who rules without requiring intercourse would have his ruling unenforced because it contradicts the established Sunnah and consensus. The strength of the evidence makes such a ruling unacceptable, even if the judge's ijtihad might be excused.

Key Terms
عَسِيلة ('usaylah): Diminutive of 'asal (honey); used metaphorically in the hadith to refer to the pleasure of sexual intercourse. From its diminutive form, Hanafi scholars infer that full satisfaction (including ejaculation) is not required.
تحليل (tahlil): The act of making a thrice-divorced woman lawful for her first husband through marriage to a second husband who consummates the marriage and then divorces her.
زيادة على الكتاب (ziyadah 'ala al-kitab): Adding a legal ruling that is not explicitly mentioned in the Quran, based on a hadith. In this context, the hadith adds the requirement of intercourse to the Quranic ruling of marriage.
خبر مشهور (khabar mashhur): A hadith that is narrated by at least three chains in every generation, but not reaching tawatur. In Hanafi usul, it can add to the Quran.
إجماع الصحابة (ijma' al-sahabah): Consensus of the Companions of the Prophet on requiring intercourse for tahlil. This is cited as the first defense to elevate the hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what is required for tahlil (making a thrice-divorced woman lawful to her first husband)?
A) Only a valid marriage contract with a second husband
B) A valid marriage contract plus full sexual intercourse including ejaculation
C) A valid marriage contract plus any sexual intercourse, even if sinful or incomplete
D) A valid marriage contract and the intention of never remarrying the first husband

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi requirement of intercourse in tahlil is defended by either companion consensus or the mashhur status of the hadith, illustrating how usul principles accommodate apparent additions to the Quran.

Two Arguments for Requiring Intercourse in Tahlil
Response to objection that hadith adds to Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two arguments used by Hanafis to require intercourse in tahlil and explain why a judge's ruling contrary to them is not enforceable.

Core Idea
Intercourse in tahlil is required by ijma and mashhur hadith; a judge cannot contradict this evidence.

This passage addresses a critical dispute in family law: can a thrice-divorced woman be remarried to her first husband without consummation of the second marriage? The Hanafi school insists on intercourse, and the text provides two proofs. Understanding these arguments is essential for grasping how Hanafi usul allows additions to the Quran through ijma and mashhur hadith.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: tahlil requires actual intercourse; mere marriage and divorce without consummation do not make the woman lawful for the first husband.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opponent's objection
Some scholars (e.g., Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib and likely Shafi'is) argue that the Quran (2:230) only mentions marriage, not intercourse, and that ahad hadith cannot add to the Quran.
The objection is based on the principle that the Quran is qat'i and cannot be specified by zanni evidence.
3
Analyse the first Hanafi response: Ijma
The Companions unanimously required intercourse, as transmitted by Ibn Abi Shayba. The objection from Sa'id is dismissed as due to unawareness of the ijma or the hadith.
This argument relies on the principle that ijma of the Companions is a binding proof.
4
Analyse the second Hanafi response: Mashhur hadith
The hadith of al-'Usaylah is considered mashhur, which in Hanafi usul can add to the Quran. The text acknowledges the objection that it is technically ahad but argues that the ummah's acceptance elevates it.
The passage notes the weakness of the 'ummah's acceptance' argument, showing scholarly nuance.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis require intercourse; others do not. A judge ruling otherwise is not enforceable, and a mufti cannot give a contrary fatwa after the evidence is clear.
This underscores the seriousness of the ruling.

فيكون التحليل بدون الوطءِ مخالفاً للحديث المشهور، حتّى لو قضى القاضي به لا ينفذ. وأجابوا عنه بوجهين : الوجه الأول : وهو أولاهما : إنّ هذا الحديث تأيد بالإجماع، فإنّ الصحابة أجمعوا على اشتراط الوطء، وقد ثبت هذا نصاً عن ابن مسعود وأنس وأبي هريرة وعلي وغيرهم على ما أخرجه ابن أبي شيبة في مصنفه، ولم يعلم له مخالف في ذلك الصدر، فتصح الزيادة به على الكتاب. فإن قلت: لو تحقق الإجماع لم يخالفه سعيد بن المسيب؟ وهو من كبار التابعين الآخذين عن كبار الصحابة. قلت : لعله لم يصل إليه خبر هذا الإجماع ولم يصل إليه حديث العسيلة، وإلا لم يخالف، ولا بعد في أنّ لا يصل خبر بعض الجزئيات إلى بعض الأكابر ففوق كل ذي علم عليم، ومن علم حجّة على من لم يعلم عند كل ذي عقل سليم. الوجه الثاني : ما اختاره صاحب «الهداية» وتبعه الشارح وغيره : إن حديث العسيلة من الأخبار المشهورة، والخبر المشهور تجوز به الزيادة على الكتاب، كما تقرر في علم الأصول، وأورد عليه أنه كونه مشهوراً بالمعنى اللغوي مسلّم. وأما بالمعنى الاصطلاحي الذي تجوز به الزيادة فممنوع، بل الصحيح أنه مع شهرته من أخبار الآحاد لم يصل إلى درجة التواتر ولا إلى درجة الشهرة، إلا أن يقال : هذا الحديث لما تلقته الأمة بالقبول فالمخالف فيه شاذ لم يعتد به، صار في حكم المشهور، ولا يخفى وهنه، فإنّ تلقي الأمة بقبول حديث والعمل على وفقه لا يخرجه من حيز أخبار الآحاد، ولا يدخله في المشهور الاصطلاحي. [١] قوله : لو قضى القاضي به ؛ أي بالتحليل بدون الوطء، ووجه عدم نفاذ القضاء فيه أنه مخالف لما دلّت عليه السنّة وأجمع عليه جمهور الأمة، بل نطقت به إشارة الآية، ومن شدّ فيه شدّ عن طريق سلف الأمة، وهو وإن كان معذوراً في حكمه باجتهاده، فالقاضي لا يكون معذوراً في القضاء، والمفتي في الإفتاء به بعد وضوح الدلائل وسطوع الوسائل.
So tahlil without intercourse is contrary to the famous hadith, such that even if a judge ruled by it, it would not be enforced. And they responded to it with two aspects: The first aspect, and it is the more correct of the two: that this hadith is supported by ijma, for the Companions agreed upon the condition of intercourse, and this has been textually established from Ibn Mas'ud, Anas, Abu Hurayra, Ali, and others, as transmitted by Ibn Abi Shayba in his Musannaf, and no opponent is known among that early generation, so addition to the Book is valid by it. If you say: If ijma were established, Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib would not have opposed it, and he is among the great Followers who took from the great Companions. I say: Perhaps the news of this ijma did not reach him, nor did the hadith of al-'Usaylah reach him; otherwise he would not have opposed. It is not unlikely that news of some particulars does not reach some great persons, for above every possessor of knowledge is the All-Knowing, and whoever knows is a proof against whoever does not know, according to every possessor of sound intellect. The second aspect: what the author of al-Hidayah chose, followed by the commentator and others: that the hadith of al-'Usaylah is among the mashhur narrations, and a mashhur narration permits addition to the Book, as established in Usul al-Fiqh. It was objected that its being mashhur in the linguistic sense is conceded, but in the technical sense that permits addition it is denied; rather, the correct view is that despite its fame, it is ahad, not reaching the level of tawatur nor the level of mashhur, except that it is said: this hadith, since the ummah received it with acceptance and the one who opposes it is anomalous and disregarded, it becomes in the ruling of mashhur. But its weakness is not hidden, for the ummah's acceptance of a hadith and acting according to it does not remove it from the realm of ahad narrations nor enter it into the technical mashhur. [1] His saying: 'even if a judge ruled by it'; i.e., by tahlil without intercourse, and the reason for the non-enforcement of the ruling is that it contradicts what the Sunnah indicates and what the majority of the ummah have agreed upon; rather, the allusion of the verse speaks of it. Whoever insists on it deviates from the path of the predecessors of the ummah, and although he may be excused in his ijtihad, the judge is not excused in passing judgment, nor the mufti in giving a fatwa with it after the evidences have become clear and the means have become apparent.

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the requirement of actual intercourse for tahlil (making a thrice-divorced woman lawful to her first husband). The text presents two arguments supporting that the hadith of al-'Usaylah – which requires intercourse – is a valid addition to the Quranic verse (2:230) that mentions only remarriage without explicit intercourse. The first argument relies on ijma of the Companions, citing multiple transmitted statements. The objection from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib is addressed by stating that he may not have been aware of the ijma or the hadith. The second argument, from al-Hidayah, holds that the hadith is mashhur (well-known), and according to Hanafi usul, a mashhur narration can add to the Quran. The objection that it is technically ahad is countered by noting that the ummah's acceptance elevates it to the status of mashhur, though the text acknowledges the weakness of this claim. The footnote explains that a judge's ruling contrary to the established evidence is not enforceable. All arguments uphold the Hanafi position that intercourse is necessary for tahlil.

Key Terms
التحليل (al-tahlil): The act of making a thrice-divorced woman lawful for her first husband by her marrying and being divorced by a second husband.
المشهور (al-mashhur): A hadith that is widely transmitted but not to the level of tawatur; in Hanafi usul, it can add to the Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The ijma of the Companions
C) Analogy with similar cases

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires intercourse for tahlil based on the ijma of the Companions and the mashhur hadith of al-'Usaylah, and a judge cannot issue a ruling contrary to this established evidence.

Tahlil by an Adolescent Boy (Murahiq) is Valid
Ruling that a minor near puberty can effect tahlil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tahlil by an adolescent boy and explain the evidence from the hadith of al-'Usaylah.

Core Idea
An adolescent boy can perform tahlil if he experiences pleasure; puberty is not required.

This lesson examines the validity of tahlil when performed by a boy nearing puberty. While many assume the second husband must be an adult, the Hanafi school holds that a murahiq suffices as long as he experiences pleasure during intercourse. The proof is drawn from the hadith of al-'Usaylah, which emphasizes tasting the sweetness of intercourse, a condition that does not require full maturity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is tahlil (making a thrice-divorced woman lawful for her first husband) performed by an adolescent boy (murahiq). The ruling is that it is valid (sahih).
The passage explicitly states: 'والمراهق يحلل'.
2
Locate the Dalil
The proof is the hadith of al-'Usaylah (حديث العسيلة), a hadith from the Sunnah. The passage references it generally, indicating the requirement of pleasure (ذوق العسيلة).
The hadith is zanni al-thubut but qati' al-dalala in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The hadith requires 'tasting the sweetness' of intercourse. This implies the experience of pleasure, not merely penetration or puberty. An adolescent with desire and erection can achieve pleasure, so he qualifies as muhallil.
The passage contrasts this with mere insertion like a kohl stick into a kohl container.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
Some other schools require puberty for the second husband. The Hanafi position is based on the broader interpretation of pleasure.
Cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih.
5
Evaluate the Rejection of the Trick
The passage rejects a trick where a woman marries a senseless boy only for insertion without pleasure. Such a marriage does not fulfill the condition of pleasure and is invalid.
This reinforces that the essence is mutual pleasure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(والمراهق يحلل لا سيدها ) : المراهق هو صبي قارب البلوغ، ويجامعُ مثله، ولا بد من أن يتحرك آلته ، ويشتهي. [١]قوله : والمراهق يحلل ؛ لإطلاق حديث العسيلة، فإنّه يقتضي أنّ المحلل وطء الثاني بحيث تحصل اللذة، وهو موجود في الصبي الذي لم يبلغ مبلغ الرجال، لكن يتحرك ذكره بالشهوة، ويطأ مثله فلا يشترط في المحلل البلوغ، وأشار بقيد المراهق إلى أنه لا يكفي تحليل من دونه. وذكر بعض أصحاب الفتاوى : حيلة لامرأة تستحي من وطئ الثاني وتريد العود إلى الأول، وهي أن تنكح صبيّاً لا تمييز له، ويدخلُ ذكره في فرجها ويحركها فتحـلّ للأول، وهذا باطل، فإنّ الشرط هو ذوق لذة الجماع من الطرفين، بنص الحديث، لا مجرد إدخال الذكر في الفرج كإدخال الميل في المكحلة. [٢] قوله : لا سيدها ؛ يعني لا يكفي وطأه للتحليل ، فلو طلق زوج الأمة زوجته فوطئها سيدها بحكم ملك اليمين، لا تحل للزوج الأوّل ؛ لأن الشرط في التحليل أن تنكح زوجاً غيره لا أن تطأ رجلاً غيره.
(And the adolescent boy effects tahlil, not her master): The adolescent is a boy nearing puberty, who can have intercourse like him, and it is necessary that his organ moves and he desires. [1] His saying: 'The adolescent boy effects tahlil' because of the general application of the hadith of al-'Usaylah, for it requires that the tahlil be the intercourse of the second husband such that pleasure is obtained, and that is present in a boy who has not reached the level of men but his penis moves with desire and he has intercourse like him; so puberty is not required in the one who performs tahlil. And he indicated by the restriction 'adolescent' that the tahlil of one below that is not sufficient. And some of the authors of fatwas mentioned a trick for a woman who is shy of intercourse with the second husband and wants to return to the first: that she marry a boy with no discernment, and his penis enters her vagina and he moves her, so she becomes lawful for the first. But this is false, for the condition is the tasting of the pleasure of intercourse by both parties, according to the text of the hadith, not merely the insertion of the penis into the vagina like inserting a kohl stick into a kohl container. [2] His saying: 'not her master' means that his intercourse does not suffice for tahlil. Thus, if a husband divorces his slave wife, and then her master has intercourse with her by virtue of right hand ownership, she does not become lawful for the first husband, because the condition in tahlil is that she marry another husband, not that she have intercourse with another man.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This is a ruling that an adolescent boy (murahiq) can validly perform tahlil, while the master of a slave woman cannot. The text defines murahiq as a boy nearing puberty who is capable of intercourse with desire and erection. The proof is the hadith of al-'Usaylah, which requires 'tasting' the pleasure of intercourse; this can occur with an adolescent. Thus, puberty is not a condition. The text rejects a deceptive trick where a woman marries a senseless boy merely for insertion without pleasure; such insertion is insufficient. Additionally, if a woman is a slave and her master has intercourse with her after her husband's divorce, that does not make her lawful for the first husband because she must marry a different husband, not simply have intercourse with another man.

Key Terms
المراهق (al-murahiq): A boy nearing puberty who is capable of intercourse with desire and erection.
المحلل (al-muhallil): The second husband who marries a thrice-divorced woman and makes her lawful for the first husband by divorcing her after consummation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is an adolescent boy without puberty considered valid for tahlil?
A) Because he is legally an adult
B) Because pleasure can be attained
C) Because he is the master
D) Because he has reached the age of discernment

Key Takeaway
An adolescent boy with desire and erection can validly perform tahlil because the required pleasure can be attained without full puberty.

Marriage with Condition of Tahlil is Makruh Tahrimi
Ruling on marriage intended solely for tahlil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marriage with the condition of tahlil and explain its proof from hadith.

Core Idea
Marriage with explicit tahlil condition is valid but sinful, cursed by Allah.

This passage addresses a sensitive issue: a marriage intended solely to make a thrice-divorced woman lawful for her first husband. The Hanafi school rules such a marriage prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) when the condition is verbally stated, based on a clear hadith. We will examine the ruling, its proof, and the distinction between explicit condition and hidden intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is marriage contracted with the condition of tahlil. According to the passage, the ruling is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
The marriage contract itself remains valid but the condition makes it sinful.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith: 'Allah cursed the muhallil and the one for whom tahlil is done.' This hadith is reported by several major hadith collections.
The curse indicates a strong prohibition.
3
Analyze the dalil's authority and meaning
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning (dalala) is clear in condemning the act. Hanafis classify the ruling as makruh tahrimi because the evidence is zanni.
If the evidence were qat'i, it would be haram.
4
Distinguish explicit condition from hidden intention
The dislike applies only when the condition is verbally expressed in the contract. If it is merely intended in the heart without verbal stipulation, it is not disliked according to the majority of scholars.
This is a crucial practical distinction.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: the marriage is valid, so children are legitimate, and a divorce is required to end it. The sin lies in the condition, not the contract itself.
Some early scholars permitted it entirely, but the Hanafi position is the relied-upon view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكره النكاح بشرط التحليل(۱) هو [٣] قوله : وكره النكاح ؛ أي لو نكح امرأة بشرط أن يطأها فيطلقها لتعود إلى الأول يكون ذلك النكاحُ مكروهاً تحريما ؛ لحديث: «لعن الله المحلل والمحلل له(۲)، أخرجه أحمد وأبو داود والترمذي وابن ماجة والبيهقي في سننه» من حديث علي. وأحمد والبيهقي وابن أبي شيبة من حديث أبي هريرة الله. (1) أي كره تحريماً بأن يقول : تزوجتك على أن أحللك، أو قالت المرأة ذلك أو وكيليها، أما لو أضمرا ذلك في قلبهما فلا يكره عند عامة العلماء. ينظر : درر الحكام»(۱ : ۳۸۷)، و(الدر المنتقى»(١ : ٤٣٩). (۲) في سنن أبي داود (۱ : ٦۳۳) ، وسنن ابن ماجة (١) : (٦۲۳)، و«السنن الصغير»(٥ : ٣۷۲)، وغيرها.
And marriage with the condition of tahlil is disapproved. [3] His saying: 'And marriage is disapproved'; that is, if a man marries a woman with the condition that he have intercourse with her and then divorce her so she returns to the first husband, that marriage is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) due to the hadith: 'Allah has cursed the muhallil and the one for whom tahlil is done,' reported by Ahmad, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah, and al-Bayhaqi from the hadith of Ali, and by Ahmad, al-Bayhaqi, and Ibn Abi Shayba from the hadith of Abu Hurayra. (1) That is, it is prohibitively disliked when he says, 'I married you on condition that I make you lawful,' or the woman or their agents say so. But if they conceal it in their hearts, it is not disliked according to the general scholars. See Durar al-Hukkam (1:387) and al-Durr al-Muntaqa (1:439). (2) In Sunan Abi Dawud (1:633), Sunan Ibn Majah (1:623), and al-Sunan al-Saghir (5:372), etc.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that a marriage contracted with the explicit condition of tahlil (i.e., the second husband marries intending to divorce the woman so she can return to her first husband) is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). The proof is the hadith cursing both the muhallil (the second husband) and the one for whom tahlil is done (the first husband or the woman). The commentary clarifies that this ruling applies when the condition is stated verbally; if the intention is merely in the heart without verbal stipulation, it is not disliked according to the majority of scholars. The sources of the hadith are provided.

Key Terms
المحلل (al-muhallil): The person who marries a woman with the intent of making her lawful for her first husband, often called a 'halala' husband.
المحلل له (al-muhallal lahu): The first husband who seeks to remarry his thrice-divorced wife after her interim marriage.
كره تحريما (kariha tahriman): Prohibitively disliked; an act that is sinful but not as severe as haram; it is closer to haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does a marriage with the condition of tahlil become makruh tahrimi according to the passage?
A) When the intention is hidden in the heart
B) When the condition is verbally expressed
C) When the marriage is not consummated
D) When the first husband is unaware

Key Takeaway
Marriage with an explicit condition of tahlil is valid but prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) because of the hadith cursing the muhallil.

The Murahiq as a Valid Muhallil
Explains legal capacity of minor for tahlil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a murahiq to serve as muhallil and distinguish valid tahlil from invalid tricks.

Core Idea
A boy who can experience desire suffices for tahlil; mere insertion does not.

A common question in tahlil is whether a minor can serve as the second husband. The Hanafi school addresses this by examining the requirement of the hadith of 'usaylah: pleasure in intercourse. This passage clarifies that a boy nearing puberty (murahiq) can fulfill that role, but a younger child cannot. It also warns against a fraudulent trick that some later scholars proposed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The passage addresses whether a minor can serve as a muhallil for tahlil. The Hanafi school provides a nuanced ruling.
The issue is not about a child generally, but specifically a murahiq.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The author cites the hadith of al-'usaylah, which indicates that tahlil requires intercourse that produces pleasure. Find the exact phrasing in the source.
The hadith is a general statement (itlaq) that sets the condition.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith proves that pleasure must be attained. The author argues that a murahiq can experience and give pleasure, so the condition is met. Show how 'pleasure' is defined.
The key is that the murahiq's penis moves with desire and he can have intercourse like an adult.
4
Identify the condition and its limit
The author states that a child younger than murahiq (i.e., non-discerning) cannot serve. The condition is capacity for desire, not puberty.
This distinguishes the Hanafi view from potential stricter views.
5
Evaluate the invalid trick
Some fatwa writers proposed a trick where a woman marries a non-discerning infant. The author rejects it because it violates the hadith condition of mutual pleasure.
The analogy to a kohl stick shows mere insertion is insufficient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : والمراهق يحلل ؛ لإطلاق حديث العسيلة، فإنّه يقتضي أنّ المحلل وطء الثاني بحيث تحصل اللذة، وهو موجود في الصبي الذي لم يبلغ مبلغ الرجال، لكن يتحرك ذكره بالشهوة، ويطأ مثله فلا يشترط في المحلل البلوغ، وأشار بقيد المراهق إلى أنه لا يكفي تحليل من دونه. وذكر بعض أصحاب الفتاوى : حيلة لامرأة تستحي من وطئ الثاني وتريد العود إلى الأول، وهي أن تنكح صبيّاً لا تمييز له، ويدخلُ ذكره في فرجها ويحركها فتحلّ للأول، وهذا باطل، فإنّ الشرط هو ذوق لذة الجماع من الطرفين، بنص الحديث، لا مجرد إدخال الذكر في الفرج كإدخال الميل في المكحلة.
He said: The murahiq makes [the woman] halal because of the general import of the hadith of al-'usaylah, which requires that the muhallil's intercourse be such that pleasure is attained. This exists in a boy who has not reached the level of men but whose male organ moves with desire and who has intercourse with someone like him. So puberty is not a condition for the muhallil. And he indicated by the qualifier 'murahiq' that the tahlil by one younger than that is not sufficient. Some fatwa writers mentioned a trick for a woman who is shy of intercourse with the second [husband] and wants to return to the first: that she marry a non-discerning boy, and his penis enters her vagina and he moves her, so she becomes halal for the first. This is invalid, for the condition [according to the text of the hadith] is tasting the pleasure of intercourse from both sides, not merely inserting the penis into the vagina like inserting a kohl stick into a kohl container.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The passage explains that a murahiq (a boy who has almost reached puberty and can experience sexual desire) can serve as a muhallil in tahlil. The proof is the hadith of al-'usaylah, which indicates that the condition for tahlil is that the second husband has intercourse that produces pleasure. This can be achieved by a boy who has desire and can physically perform intercourse, so puberty is not necessary. The author distinguishes between a murahiq and a younger child, as the latter cannot provide the required pleasure. The passage then rejects a fraudulent trick (hila) mentioned by some later scholars, where a woman marries a non-discerning infant. This is invalid because the hadith explicitly requires the tasting of pleasure from both parties, not mere insertion.

Key Terms
مراهق (murāhiq): A boy who has nearly reached puberty, whose penis moves with desire and who can engage in intercourse with a woman like him.
محلل (muḥallil): The man who marries a triply divorced woman temporarily to make her permissible for her first husband.
عسيلة (ʿusayla): A hadith where the Prophet ﷺ compared the condition of tahlil to tasting honey, indicating that the second husband must actually taste the pleasure of intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He must be an adult male.
B) He must have reached puberty.
C) His penis must move with desire and he must be able to have intercourse with a woman like him.
D) He must be at least ten years old.

Key Takeaway
The condition for a muhallil is the capacity to experience and give pleasure during intercourse, not puberty or adulthood; a murahiq satisfies this condition.

The Master's Intercourse Does Not Serve as Tahlil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a master's intercourse with his slave woman does not constitute tahlil and identify the correct condition for tahlil.

Core Idea
Tahlil requires marriage, not mere intercourse.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling from the Hanafi school: does a master's intercourse with his own slave woman, after she is divorced by her husband, make her halal for the first husband? The answer is a clear no, because the condition for tahlil is that she marry another husband (nikah), not merely have intercourse with another man. This distinction is crucial for understanding the legal definition of tahlil.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal consequence
The act is a master having intercourse with his own slave woman after her husband divorced her. The desired consequence is that she becomes halal for the first husband (tahlil).
2
Identify the condition for tahlil
The author states the condition explicitly: 'that she marry another husband' (an tankaha zawjan ghayrahu). This means a valid marriage contract (nikah) is required.
The Arabic 'tankaha' implies a full marriage, not just intercourse.
3
Compare the act to the condition
The master's intercourse is by right of ownership (milk yamin), not through marriage. Therefore, it does not fulfill the condition of marrying another husband.
Ownership and marriage are distinct legal categories in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Derive the ruling
Since the condition is not met, the master's intercourse does not make the woman halal for her first husband. She remains haram for him until she properly marries another man and is divorced.
This ruling is a straightforward application of the condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : لا سيدها ؛ يعني لا يكفي وطأه للتحليل ، فلو طلق زوج الأمة زوجته فوطئها سيدها بحكم ملك اليمين، لا تحل للزوج الأوّل ؛ لأن الشرط في التحليل أن تنكح زوجاً غيره لا أن تطأ رجلاً غيره.
He said: Not her master – meaning, his intercourse is not sufficient for tahlil. So if the husband of a slave woman divorces his wife, and then her master has intercourse with her by virtue of his right of ownership, she does not become halal for the first husband because the condition for tahlil is that she marry another husband, not that she have intercourse with another man.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This is a simple ruling statement. The author explains that the master's intercourse with his own slave woman does not constitute tahlil, even after she is divorced by her husband. The reason is that tahlil specifically requires marriage (nikah) to a second man, not just any sexual intercourse. The master's intercourse is by right of ownership (milk yamin), which is not a marriage. Therefore, the woman remains haram for the first husband until she marries another man and is properly divorced.

Key Terms
ملك اليمين (milk al-yamīn): Right of ownership over a slave, which gives the master the right to sexual intercourse without marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) No, because the master's intercourse is not marriage.
C) Yes, if the master intends to make her halal.
D) No, only if the master marries her first.

Key Takeaway
The master's intercourse does not serve as tahlil because tahlil requires marriage (nikah), not any form of intercourse.
