Marriage with Condition of Tahlil: Ruling and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on marriage with tahlil condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a marriage conditioned for tahlil, explain the disagreement between Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, and evaluate Ibn Qayyim's contradictory view.

Core Idea
A marriage with explicit tahlil condition is valid but sinful; the woman becomes halal only after proper divorce without condition.

This passage addresses a delicate issue: a man marrying a woman with the express intention to divorce her so she can return to her first husband after a triple divorce. The Hanafi school distinguishes between the validity of the contract and its sinfulness. The text presents the leading Hanafi positions and forcefully rejects the extreme view of Ibn Qayyim that such a marriage is outright fornication. We will walk through the reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its basis
Identify that the marriage is makruh tahriman (prohibitively disliked) due to the hadith cursing the muhallil. Understand that the prohibition is about the condition, not the marriage itself.
The hadith is cited as evidence of sin, not invalidity.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Note that Muhammad al-Shaybani holds the marriage valid (sahih) but sinful, and the woman does not become halal for the first via this intercourse. Abu Yusuf holds the marriage invalid because it resembles mut'a.
The difference affects the immediate consequence for the woman.
3
Understand the opposing Hanbali view
Ibn Qayyim argues the marriage is absolutely invalid (batil) and amounts to fornication, citing the same hadith.
This is a radical position within the tradition.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The author dismisses Ibn Qayyim's view as having no proof, upholding the Hanafi position that the condition does not invalidate the contract but makes it sinful.
The principle: invalid conditions do not corrupt a valid marriage contract.
5
Determine the practical consequence
According to the mufta bihi (Muhammad's view), after the second husband divorces her without condition and she completes 'idda, she becomes halal for the first husband. This is the thamarah al-khilaf.
Thus the woman is not trapped; but the act carries sin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وكره النكاح ; أي لو نكح امرأة بشرط أن يطأها فيطلقها لتعود إلى الأول يكون ذلك النكاحُ مكروهاً تحريما ؛ لحديث: «لعن الله المحلل والمحـلـل لـه»، أخرجه أحمد وأبو داود والترمذي وابن ماجة والبَيْهَقِي في سننه من حديث علي. وأحمد والبيهقي وابن أبي شيبة من حديث أبي هريرة الله.
كتاب الطلاق باب الرجعة [١) قوله : وتحل للأول ; يعني لو نكحها بشرط التحليل، فوطئها وطلقها فبعد العدة تحل للأول، وإن لزم الإثم بمثل هذا النكاح والتحليل، وفيه خلاف : فعند محمد ه : إنّه يصح النكاح بشرط التحليل ، لما تقرر في مقره : أن النكاح لا يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة، ولا تحلّ على الأوّل بمثل هذا الوطء ؛ لأنه استعجل ما أخره الشرع، فإنّ الشرع أخر حلّها على الأوّل إلى موت الثاني أو طلاقه، فيجازى بمنع مقصوده. وعن أبي يوسف له : إنه يبطل النكاح بشرط التحليل ؛ لأنه في معنى المؤقت، وهو نكاح باطل.
وتحل للأول، والزوج الثاني يهدمُ ما دون الثلاث، فَمَن طُلقت دونَها وتحل للأول ، والزوج الثاني يهدمُ ما دون الثلاث، فمَن طُلِّقَتْ دونَها وعن ابن مسعود : لعن رسول الله المحلل والمحلل له، أخرجه أحمد والترمذي والنسائي، ومثله عن جابر ، أخرجه الترمذي، وعن ابن عباس أخرجه ابن ماجة. وعند ابن ماجة والحاكم والبيهقي عن عقبة قال رسول الله : «ألا أخبركم بالتيس المستعار ؟ قالوا : بلى يا رسول الله قال : هو المحلّل والمحلل له ، وفي الباب آثار كثيرة من الصحابة الله توافق هذه الأخبار وأخبار أخر أيضاً. وقد بسط الكلام فيها شمس الدين ابن القيم الحنبلي تلميذ ابن تيمية الحنبلي في كتابه «إغاثة اللهفان» ، وفي كتابه زاد المعاد في هدى خير العباد»، ومال إلى عدم صحة نكاح المحلّل مطلقاً، وفساده من أصله، وكونه سفاحاً، وهو مذهب مردود لا دليل عليه.
He said: And marriage is disliked – i.e., if a man marries a woman with the condition that he will have intercourse with her and then divorce her so that she may return to the first [husband], that marriage is makruh tahriman because of the hadith: 'Allah curses the muhallil and the one for whom tahlil is done,' reported by Ahmad, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah, and al-Bayhaqi in their Sunan from the hadith of Ali, and by Ahmad, al-Bayhaqi, and Ibn Abi Shayba from the hadith of Abu Hurayra. The Book of Divorce, Chapter of Raj'a (return): He said: And she becomes halal for the first husband – meaning, if he marries her with the condition of tahlil, and then has intercourse with her and divorces her, then after the 'idda she becomes halal for the first husband, although there is sin in such a marriage and tahlil. There is disagreement: According to Muhammad, the marriage with the condition of tahlil is valid, because it is established that a marriage is not invalidated by invalid conditions, and she does not become halal for the first husband through such intercourse, because he hastened what the Law has delayed, for the Law delays her being halal for the first until the death of the second or his divorce, so he is punished by being prevented from his objective. According to Abu Yusuf, the marriage with the condition of tahlil is invalid because it is akin to a temporary marriage (mut'a), which is invalid. And she marries another husband, not just have intercourse with another man. And she needs an 'idda. And she becomes halal for the first after the 'idda. And the second husband destroys what is less than three [divorces]. So whoever is divorced less than three... And from Ibn Mas'ud: The Messenger of Allah cursed the muhallil and the one for whom tahlil is done, reported by Ahmad, al-Tirmidhi, and al-Nasa'i. Similarly from Jabir, reported by al-Tirmidhi, and from Ibn 'Abbas reported by Ibn Majah. And according to Ibn Majah, al-Hakim, and al-Bayhaqi from 'Uqba: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Shall I not tell you about the borrowed he-goat?' They said: Yes, O Messenger of Allah. He said: 'It is the muhallil and the one for whom tahlil is done.' And there are many other authentic reports from the Companions supporting these. Shams al-Din Ibn Qayyim al-Hanbali, the student of Ibn Taymiyya, has discussed them extensively in his book 'Ighathat al-Lahfan' and in his book 'Zad al-Ma'ad fi Huda Khayr al-'Ibad', and he inclined to the opinion that the marriage of the muhallil is absolutely invalid, null from the beginning, and that it is fornication, but this is a rejected opinion with no proof.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute (within Hanafi school and also with Ibn Qayyim). It first states the ruling that marriage with the explicit condition of tahlil is makruh tahriman (prohibitively disliked) because of the hadith cursing the muhallil. The text then presents the intra-Hanafi disagreement: Muhammad says the marriage is valid despite the invalid condition, because in Hanafi law, invalid conditions do not nullify the marriage contract. However, due to the sin, the woman does not become halal for the first husband through this intercourse; she remains haram as a punishment. Abu Yusuf says the marriage is completely invalid because it resembles mut'a (temporary marriage), which is batil. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the marriage is valid but sinful, and she becomes halal after the second husband divorces her without condition and she completes 'idda. The passage then cites multiple hadith supporting the prohibition, and finally refutes Ibn Qayyim's opinion that the marriage is absolutely invalid and amounts to fornication. The author dismisses Ibn Qayyim's view as having no proof.

Key Terms
تحليل (taḥlīl): The act of making a previously divorced woman lawful for her first husband through a second marriage and divorce.
مكروه تحريماً (makrūh taḥrīman): A category between haram and makruh tanzihan; prohibited but not with qat'i evidence, yet carries sin.
تيس مستعار (tays mustaʿār): A borrowed he-goat; a metaphor used by the Prophet ﷺ for the muhallil, indicating he is used for his sexual service.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (Muhammad's view), what is the effect of a marriage contracted with the explicit condition of tahlil on the woman's ability to remarry her first husband?
A) She becomes halal immediately after the second husband divorces her.
B) She does not become halal through that intercourse; she must wait for a proper divorce without condition.
C) She never becomes halal for the first husband.
D) She becomes halal only if the second husband dies.

Key Takeaway
A marriage with an explicit condition of tahlil is valid (sahih) but sinful (makruh tahriman); the woman only becomes halal for the first husband after a proper divorce without condition and completion of 'idda.

Ruling on Tahlil Marriage and Demolition of Divorces
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of conditional marriage for tahlil and its effect on divorce count.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi ruling on a tahlil marriage and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding its effect on permissibility and divorce count.

Core Idea
A tahlil marriage is valid but sinful; the woman becomes permissible for the first husband despite the intention.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah addresses a contentious issue: a marriage contracted with the explicit condition of making the wife legal for her former husband after a triple divorce. The Hanafi school maintains that such a marriage is valid, though the act is sinful, and the woman indeed becomes permissible. This position is clarified in contrast to the views of Imams Muhammad and Abu Yusuf within the school, and the relied-upon ruling is established through careful analysis of the hadith and principles of contract validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal categorization
Determine what act is being discussed (marriage with condition of tahlil) and its general legal status (valid but sinful).
The act is a marriage contract; the condition is corrupt but does not invalidate the contract.
2
State the general Hanafi principle on corrupt conditions
The text states that marriage is not invalidated by corrupt conditions. This is a key principle that supports validity.
Refer to the known Hanafi rule: al-nikah la yabtul bi al-shurut al-fasidah.
3
Outline the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Identify the three positions: Abu Hanifa (relied-upon): valid and permissible; Muhammad: valid but permissibility withheld; Abu Yusuf: invalid.
Memorize the ikhtilaf: Azim (Abu Hanifa), Muhammad, Abu Yusuf.
4
Analyze the hadith and its legal import
The hadith curses the muhallil and the one for whom tahlil is done. Discuss how the Hanafi school interprets this: the curse indicates sin, not invalidity of the contract.
The hadith does not state that the marriage is null; it only condemns the intention.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its practical effect
The relied-upon view is that of Abu Hanifa: marriage valid, woman becomes permissible, and the second husband demolishes the remaining divorces (hadm).
Practical consequence: the woman returns to the first husband with three divorces remaining.

كتاب الطلاق باب الرجعة
وتحل للأول، والزوج الثاني يهدمُ ما دون الثلاث، فمَن طُلقت دونَها وتحل للأول ، والزوج الثاني يهدمُ ما دون الثلاث، فمَن طُلِّقَتْ دونَها وعن ابن مسعود : لعن رسول الله المحلل والمحلل له، أخرجه أحمد والترمذي والنسائي، ومثله عن جابر ، أخرجه الترمذي، وعن ابن عباس أخرجه ابن ماجة. وعند ابن ماجة والحاكم والبيهقي عن عقبة قال رسول الله : «ألا أخبركم بالتيس المستعار ؟ قالوا : بلى يا رسول الله قال : هو المحلّل والمحلل له ، وفي الباب آثار كثيرة من الصحابة توافق هذه الأخبار وأخبار أخر أيضاً.
وقد بسط الكلام فيها شمس الدين ابن القيم الحنبلي تلميذ ابن تيمية الحنبلي في كتابه «إغاثة اللهفان (٣) ، وفي كتابه زاد المعاد في هدى خير العباد»، ومال إلى عدم صحة نكاح المحلّل مطلقاً، وفساده من أصله، وكونه سفاحاً، وهو مذهب مردود لا دليل عليه.
[١) قوله : وتحل للأول ؛ يعني لو نكحها بشرط التحليل، فوطئها وطلقها فبعد العدة تحل للأول، وإن لزم الإثم بمثل هذا النكاح والتحليل، وفيه خلاف : فعند محمد : إنّه يصح النكاح بشرط التحليل ، لما تقرر في مقره : أن النكاح لا يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة، ولا تحلّ على الأوّل بمثل هذا الوطء ؛ لأنه استعجل ما أخره الشرع، فإنّ الشرع أخر حلّها على الأوّل إلى موت الثاني أو طلاقه، فيجازى بمنع مقصوده.
وعن أبي يوسف : إنه يبطل النكاح بشرط التحليل ؛ لأنه في معنى المؤقت، وهو نكاح باطل.
ونحن نقول : لَمَّا كان النكاحُ لا يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة، ولا يضر في صحة إضمار الافتراض بعد مدة معينة، ولا التصريح به صح النكاح في هذه الصورة، وبينه وبين المؤقت الذي ينتهي بانتهاء الوقت بون بعيد كما مر بحثه في بحث نكاح المتعة والمؤقت.
ثم بعد النكاح الوطء يكون محلّلاً لا محالة، فإنّ الثابت في الحديث هو أنّ وطء الزوج الثاني وذوق اللذة محلل على أي وجه كان، غاية ما في الباب أن يكون مثل هذا النكاح والـوطء بعده مكروهاً تحريماً أو محرّماً ، وهو لا يمنع ترتب الأثر الشرعي، فإنّ السبب يرتبط بالمسبب، ويفيد أثره ، وإن كان على طريقة غير شرعية.
[1]قوله : خلافاً لمحمد رجّحه ابن الهمام في «فتح القدير» و«تحرير الأصول» وتبعه ابن أمير حاج الحلبي، وصاحب «البحر» و«النهر» وغيرهم، ونقل قاسم بن قُطلُوبُغا ترجيح قولهما عن جمع من المشايخ.
قال ابن الهمام في «الفتح»: «المسألة مختلفة بين الصحابة ، فروى محمد عن أبي حنيفة عن حماد . عن سعيد بن جبير قال : «كنت جالساً عند عبد الله بن عتبة بن مسعود فجاءه أعرابي فسأله عن رجلٍ طلّق امرأته طلقة أو طلقتين، ثم انقضت عدتها فتزوجت زوجاً غيره، فدخل بها ثم مات عنها أو طلقها، ثم انقضت عدتها وأراد الأول أن يتزوجها على كم هي عنده ، فالتفت إلى ابن عباس ، فقال : ما تقول في هذا ؟ قال : يهدم الزوج الثاني الواحدة والثنتين، واسأل ابن عمر قال : فلقيت ابن فقال مثل ما قال ابن عباس ». وروى البيهقي عن عمر في نحوه قال : هي عنده على ما بقي ، ونحوه عن علي وأبي بن كعب وعمران بن حصين .
Book of Divorce, Chapter of Raj'a. And she becomes permissible for the first husband, and the second husband demolishes what is less than three. So whoever is divorced with less than that and becomes permissible for the first husband, and the second husband demolishes what is less than three, so whoever is divorced with less than that. And from Ibn Mas'ud: The Messenger of Allah cursed the muhallil and the one for whom tahlil is done, narrated by Ahmad, Tirmidhi, and Nasa'i; and similarly from Jabir, narrated by Tirmidhi; and from Ibn Abbas, narrated by Ibn Majah. And from Ibn Majah, Hakim, and Bayhaqi from Uqba: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Shall I inform you of the borrowed he-goat? They said: Yes, O Messenger of Allah. He said: He is the muhallil and the one for whom tahlil is done.' And in this chapter there are many athar from the Companions agreeing with these reports and other reports as well. And Shams al-Din Ibn Qayyim al-Hanbali, student of Ibn Taymiyyah al-Hanbali, has discussed it in his book 'Ighathat al-Lahfan' and in his book 'Zad al-Ma'ad', and he inclined to the absolute invalidity of the marriage of tahlil, its corruption from its root, and that it is fornication, and this is a rejected madhhab with no evidence. [1) His saying: 'And she becomes permissible for the first husband'; meaning if he marries her with the condition of tahlil, then has intercourse with her and divorces her, after the 'idda she becomes permissible for the first husband, although sin is incurred by such marriage and tahlil. And there is disagreement about it: According to Muhammad, the marriage is valid with the condition of tahlil, based on what has been established in its place: that marriage is not invalidated by corrupt conditions, but she does not become permissible for the first husband by such intercourse; because he hastened what the law delayed, for the law delayed her permissibility for the first husband until the death or divorce of the second husband, so he is punished by the prevention of his aim. And from Abu Yusuf: The marriage becomes invalid with the condition of tahlil; because it is similar to a temporary marriage, and that is an invalid marriage. And we say: Since marriage is not invalidated by corrupt conditions, and neither the concealment of the intention nor the explicit stipulation of a fixed period harms its validity, the marriage is valid in this form, and between it and a temporary marriage which ends with the end of the time there is a great distance, as previously discussed in the discussion of mut'a and temporary marriage. Then after marriage, intercourse is necessarily tahlil, for what is established in the hadith is that the intercourse of the second husband and tasting of pleasure is tahlil in whatever manner it occurs. The utmost in this matter is that such marriage and subsequent intercourse are makruh tahriman or haram, and that does not prevent the legal effect from being attached, for the cause is linked to the effect and yields its result, even if it is done in an unlegislated manner. [1] His saying: Contrary to Muhammad, Ibn al-Humam gave preponderance to it in 'Fath al-Qadir' and 'Tahrir al-Usul', and he was followed by Ibn Amir Hajj al-Halabi, and the author of 'al-Bahr' and 'al-Nahr' and others, and Qasim ibn Qutlubugha narrated the preponderance of their view from a group of mashayikh. Ibn al-Humam said in 'al-Fath': 'The issue is disputed among the Companions. Muhammad narrated from Abu Hanifa from Hammad from Sa'id ibn Jubayr who said: I was sitting with 'Abdullah ibn 'Utba ibn Mas'ud when a Bedouin came and asked him about a man who divorced his wife once or twice, then her 'idda expired, and she married another husband, then he had intercourse with her, then he died or divorced her, then her 'idda expired, and the first wanted to marry her: how many divorces does she have with him? He turned to Ibn 'Abbas and asked him. Ibn 'Abbas said: The second husband demolishes one and two. Ask Ibn 'Umar. He said: I met Ibn 'Umar and he said the same as Ibn 'Abbas.' And al-Bayhaqi narrated from 'Umar something similar: He said: She is with him on what remains. And likewise from 'Ali, Ubayy ibn Ka'b, and 'Imran ibn Husayn.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage addresses the complex Hanafi position on the validity and effect of a marriage contracted with the explicit or implicit condition of tahlil (making the wife permissible to her former husband after a triple divorce). The text opens by stating the general rule: a woman divorced less than three times becomes permissible to her first husband through a subsequent marriage and consummation, and the second husband's act 'demolishes' (yahdimu) the remaining divorces, meaning she returns to her first husband with the full set of three potential divorces. This is the position of the majority of the Hanafi school and is supported by athar (traditions) from the Companions. The text then cites a hadith condemning the muhallil (one who marries a woman with the intent of making her lawful for her first husband) and the one who arranges such a marriage, demonstrating the severe prohibition. However, the Hanafi school distinguishes between the sinfulness of the act and its legal effects. The commentary by the author (likely from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah) then details the intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Muhammad holds that the marriage is valid (since corrupt conditions do not invalidate marriage) but the woman does not become permissible to her first husband because the husband is punished for his transgression by having his aim thwarted. Imam Abu Yusuf holds the marriage invalid because the condition makes it resemble a temporary marriage (mut'a), which is invalid. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa (as reported by Abu Yusuf later?), but the text says 'we say' (the Hanafi position) that the marriage is valid and the woman becomes permissible, though the act is sinful. This is because the hadith about tahlil only declares the act sinful but does not invalidate the marriage; the legal cause (intercourse in a valid marriage) produces its legal effect (permissibility for the first husband) regardless of the evil intention. Thus, the passage concludes that the second marriage does indeed demolish the divorces, and the woman returns to her first husband with three divorces remaining, contrary to Muhammad's view. The author cites Ibn al-Humam's preponderance of this view over Muhammad's, supported by many later Hanafi authorities.

Key Terms
تحليل (tahlil): In this context, the act of marrying a woman who has been triple-divorced with the intention of making her permissible (halal) for her first husband after the second marriage ends.
هدم (hadm): The effect of the second husband's consummation on the first husband's divorces: it 'demolishes' the remaining divorces (i.e., the wife returns with three full divorces available to the first husband).
محلل (muhallil): The person who marries a woman to make her halal for her former husband (the second husband in the context of tahlil).
تيس مستعار (tays musta'ar): Literal meaning: 'borrowed he-goat'; used in the hadith as a metaphor for the muhallil, indicating his use as a tool.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, which of the following best describes the effect of a marriage contracted with the condition of tahlil?
A) The marriage is invalid, and the woman does not become permissible.
B) The marriage is valid, and the woman becomes permissible without sin.
C) The marriage is valid, and the woman becomes permissible, but the act is sinful.
D) The marriage is valid, but the woman does not become permissible.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a tahlil marriage is valid and legally effective despite being sinful; the woman returns to the first husband with full divorces remaining.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate

The Second Husband's Effect on Remaining Divorce Count (Tahlil)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on scope of tahlil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on whether the second husband demolishes fewer than three divorces, identify the proof used by each side, and explain the practical consequence (thamarah) of the difference.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: second husband gives a fresh start; Muhammad: only three divorces are demolished.

This passage addresses a disagreement within the Hanafi school about the scope of tahlil (the second husband's intercourse making a divorced woman lawful for her first husband). The issue: if a woman was divorced fewer than three times, does the second husband's consummation reset the divorce count to zero, or does the previous count carry over? Understanding this dispute is crucial for determining how many divorces a husband retains after remarriage.

Guided Path
1
State the two Hanafi positions
Clearly formulate what Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold versus what Muhammad holds. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say the second husband demolishes any number less than three; Muhammad says only three are demolished.
The passage also mentions that Muhammad's view aligns with the majority of other schools.
2
Identify the issue and the practical consequence (thamarah)
Determine the real-life difference: if a woman with two divorces remarries and is divorced once by the first husband, does she become ba'in mughallazah (needs another tahlil) or does he have more divorces left?
This is called thamarah al-khilaf.
3
Analyze the proof of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
They use the hadith calling the second husband 'muhallil' and argue via qiyas awla: if it works for the stronger prohibition of three, it should work for weaker cases.
The hadith is considered zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalalah.
4
Examine Muhammad's opposing proof
He and the other schools argue that the hadith is specific to three divorces and that the second husband's role is merely a condition (shart) for solution, not a cause (sabab) that resets everything.
The Book and Sunnah indicate that only the severe prohibition (three) requires tahlil.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its authority
Later Hanafi scholars like Ibn al-Humam preferred Muhammad's view. Thus the operative ruling for fatwa is that only three divorces are demolished; previous counts carry over.
However, a group of earlier mashayikh preferred the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعادت إليه بعد آخر عادت إليه بثلاث خلافاً لمحمد .
ونحن نقول : لَمَّا كان النكاحُ لا يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة، ولا يضر في صحة إضمار الافتراض بعد مدة معينة، ولا التصريح به صح النكاح في هذه الصورة، وبينه وبين المؤقت الذي ينتهي بانتهاء الوقت بون بعيد كما مر بحثه في بحث نكاح المتعة والمؤقت.
ثم بعد النكاح الوطء يكون محلّلاً لا محالة، فإنّ الثابت في الحديث هو أنّ وطء الزوج الثاني وذوق اللذة محلل على أي وجه كان، غاية ما في الباب أن يكون مثل هذا النكاح والـوطء بعده مكروهاً تحريماً أو محرّماً ، وهو لا يمنع ترتب الأثر الشرعي، فإنّ السبب يرتبط بالمسبب، ويفيد أثره ، وإن كان على طريقة غير شرعية.
قوله : خلافاً لمحمد الله رجّحه ابن الهمام في «فتح القدير» و«تحرير الأصول» وتبعه ابن أمير حاج الحلبي، وصاحب «البحر» و«النهر» وغيرهم، ونقل قاسم بن قُطلُوبُغا ترجيح قولهما عن جمع من المشايخ.
قال ابن الهمام في «الفتح»: «المسألة مختلفة بين الصحابة ، فروى محمد عن أبي حنيفة عن حماد . عن سعيد بن جبير الله قال : «كنت جالساً عند عبد الله بن عتبة بن مسعود فجاءه أعرابي فسأله عن رجلٍ طلّق امرأته طلقة أو طلقتين، ثم انقضت عدتها فتزوجت زوجاً غيره، فدخل بها ثم مات عنها أو طلقها، ثم انقضت عدتها وأراد الأول أن يتزوجها على كم هي عنده ، فالتفت إلى ابن عباس ، فقال : ما تقول في هذا ؟ قال : يهدم الزوج الثاني الواحدة والثنتين، واسأل ابن عمر قال : فلقيت ابن فقال مثل ما قال ابن عباس ». وروى البيهقي عن عمر ه في نحوه قال : هي عنده على ما بقي ، ونحوه عن علي وأبي بن كعب وعمران بن حصين .
والمبائنة بثلاث لو قالت : حلّلت في مدة تحتمله، وغلب على ظنه صدقها والمبائنة بثلاث لو قالت : حلّلت في مدة تحتمله، وغلب على ظنه صدقها فأخذ المشايخ من الفقهاء بقول شبّان الصحابة له ، وشبان الفقهاء بقول مشايخ الصحابة ، والترجيح بالوجه». انتهى
وتوضيح الخلاف مع دلائله أنه إذا طلق رجل زوجته واحداً أو اثنتين فتزوجت بعد عدتها زوجاً آخر، ثمّ مات هو أو طلّقها بعد الوطء، ثم نكحها الأول بعد العدة، فهل يثبت له ملك جديد كما في صورة الثلاث أم يحسب ما مضى.
عند أبي يوسف وأبي حنيفة : الزوج الثاني كما يهدم الثلاث ويثبت وطأه حلاً جديداً للأول، بحيث يملك الثلاث، كذلك يهدم ما دونه أيضاً، ويثبت حلاً جديداً. وعند محمد والشافعي ومالك وأحمد لا يهدم ، فلو طلّق في المرة الثانية واحداً بعدما كان طلقها سابقاً اثنين تصير بائنة مغلّظة، لا تحل له حتى تنكح زوجاً غيره ؛ وذلك لأن الكتاب والسنة حكما بكون وطء الزوج الثاني منهياً للحرمة الثابتة بالثلاث لا الحرمة الخفيفة.
وله : أن الزوج الثاني سمّاه النبي المحلَّل ، والمحلل من يثبت الحل، فلما كان وطؤه مثبتا للحل الجديد في الثلاث مع قوة الحرمة هناك، فلأن يثبت الحل الجديد فيما دونه مع خفة الحرمة أولى.
ويرد عليه : أنّ وطء الزوج الثاني ليس بمثبتِ حقيقة للحل الجديد، بل ثبوت الحل الجديد بالنظر إلى الأصل، ووطؤه شرط لثبوته ؛ ولذا سمي محللاً، وهذا الشرط إنما يظهر أثره في الحرمة الغليظة، ولا يلزم منه أن يكون شرطاً في الحرمة الخفيفة أيضاً ، كيف فإنّ الحلّ من وجه باق هناك، وإن شئت زيادة التفصيل فارجع إلى شروح «أصول البزدوي»، وشروح «التحرير».
And she returns to him after the last, she returns to him with three, contrary to Muhammad. And we say: Since marriage is not invalidated by corrupt conditions, nor does it harm the validity of concealing the condition after a specified period, nor explicitly stating it, marriage is valid in this case, and between it and the temporary marriage that ends with the end of time there is a great distance as discussed earlier in the discussion of mut'ah and temporary marriage. Then after marriage, intercourse inevitably becomes tahlil (making lawful), for what is established in the hadith is that the intercourse of the second husband and the tasting of pleasure is a tahlil in any case whatsoever. The most that can be said is that such marriage and intercourse thereafter is makruh tahrimi or haram, but that does not prevent the legal effect from being produced, for the cause is linked to the effect and produces its result even if it is done in a non-shar'i manner. His saying: contrary to Muhammad – may Allah have mercy on him – was preferred by Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir and Tahrir al-Usul, and followed by Ibn Amir Haj al-Halabi, and the author of al-Bahr and al-Nahr and others. And Qasim ibn Qutlubugha narrated the preference of their (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's) view from a group of mashayikh. Ibn al-Humam said in al-Fath: 'The issue is disputed among the Companions. Muhammad narrated from Abu Hanifa from Hammad from Sa'id ibn Jubayr who said: I was sitting with 'Abdullah ibn 'Utba ibn Mas'ud when a Bedouin came and asked him about a man who divorced his wife one or two times, then her 'iddah expired, and she married another husband, and he had intercourse with her, then he died or divorced her, then her 'iddah expired, and the first husband wanted to marry her – on how many (divorces) is she with him? He turned to Ibn 'Abbas and said: What do you say about this? He said: The second husband demolishes the one and the two. And ask Ibn 'Umar. He said: Then I met Ibn 'Umar and he said the same as Ibn 'Abbas.' And al-Bayhaqi narrated from 'Umar something similar: 'She is with him on what remains.' And similarly from 'Ali, Ubayy ibn Ka'b, and 'Imran ibn Husayn. And the one separated by three – if she says: I performed tahlil in a time that can accommodate it, and he strongly believes she is truthful – the mashayikh among the jurists took the saying of the young Companions, and the young jurists took the saying of the elder Companions, and preference is by weight.' End. And clarification of the dispute with its proofs: if a man divorces his wife one or two times, and she after her 'iddah marries another husband, then he dies or divorces her after intercourse, then the first husband marries her after the 'iddah – does he have a fresh ownership as in the case of three, or is what is past counted? According to Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa: just as the second husband demolishes the three and his intercourse establishes a new solution for the first such that he owns the three, similarly he demolishes what is less than that and establishes a new solution. According to Muhammad, al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad, he does not demolish. So if he divorces in the second time one, having previously divorced her two, she becomes a permanently separated woman (ba'in mughallazah), not lawful for him until she marries another husband. That is because the Book and the Sunnah ruled that the intercourse of the second husband puts an end to the prohibition established by three, not the light prohibition. And for him (Abu Hanifa): the Prophet ﷺ called the second husband 'al-muhallil', and the muhallil is one who establishes the solution. So since his intercourse establishes a new solution in the case of three despite the strength of the prohibition there, it is more appropriate that it should establish the new solution for less than that given the lightness of the prohibition. And it is replied to him: the intercourse of the second husband is not actually establishing a new solution, rather the establishment of a new solution is in relation to the original, and his intercourse is a condition for its establishment. That is why he is called muhallil. And this condition only shows its effect in the severe prohibition, and it does not follow that it is also a condition for the light prohibition – how so? For the solution remains in some respect there. And if you want more detail, refer to the commentaries on Usul al-Bazdawi and the commentaries on al-Tahrir.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of a second husband's intercourse on the remaining count of divorces. The issue: If a woman is divorced one or two revocable divorces, marries another man after her 'iddah, consummates, then returns to her first husband after the second husband's death or divorce, does she come back with a fresh set of three divorces (as if she had never been divorced before) or does the previous count carry over? The author first states the rule: 'she returns to him with three, contrary to Muhammad.' This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. The reasoning is that a marriage with a corrupt condition is still valid, and intercourse after such a marriage still counts as tahlil (making the woman lawful for the first husband). The hadith about the muhallil is cited: the second husband's intercourse makes the woman lawful for the first, regardless of how many divorces preceded. Then a note from Ibn al-Humam is quoted, showing that some later scholars (like Ibn al-Humam) preferred Muhammad's view, and that the Companions themselves differed: Ibn 'Abbas and Ibn 'Umar said the second husband demolishes one and two, while 'Umar, 'Ali, Ubayy, and 'Imran said she returns with what remains. The author then clarifies the dispute: At stake is whether a 'new ownership' (milk jadid) is established. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf analogize from the case of three divorces: since the second husband establishes a new solution for the severe prohibition of three, it is more appropriate (awla) that he does so for the lesser prohibition. Muhammad and the majority of other schools reply that the second husband's role is merely a condition (shart) for the solution, not the cause (sabab). That condition is only needed for the severe prohibition; for fewer than three, the solution remains in some sense, so no new start is given. The practical consequence: According to Muhammad, if a woman had two divorces, then after tahlil and remarriage, if the first husband divorces her once, she becomes permanently separated (ba'in mughallazah) and cannot return to him without another tahlil. According to Abu Hanifa, he would have a fresh set of three divorces. The passage ends by directing readers to more detailed works for further elaboration.

Key Terms
المحلل (al-muhallil): A man who marries a woman who has been irrevocably divorced (three times) and has intercourse with her, thereby making her lawful for her first husband to remarry. In this passage, the term is extended to cases of fewer divorces.
الهدم (al-hadm): The 'demolition' or nullification of prior divorces by the second husband's intercourse, such that the first husband obtains a fresh set of up to three divorces.
البائنة المغلظة (al-ba'in al-mughallazah): A woman who is irrevocably separated after three divorces (or after two plus one if the leftovers are completed), requiring a new marriage (tahlil) to become permissible to her ex-husband again.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the view of Muhammad al-Shaybani (as preferred by later Hanafi scholars), if a woman is divorced two revocable divorces, then after tahlil and remarriage to the first husband, if he divorces her once again, what is her status?
A) She becomes ba'in mughallazah and cannot remarry him without a new tahlil.
B) She remains with one divorce left in the new set; the second husband demolished the previous two.
C) She is still married; the divorce was invalid.
D) She becomes mubah (permissible) to marry any man.

Key Takeaway
The second husband's intercourse only demolishes three divorces according to the mufta bihi; fewer than three carry over and accumulate if further divorces occur.

Does a Second Marriage Reset Less Than Three Divorces?
Explains intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute on resetting divorce count.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on whether a second marriage after one or two divorces resets the count and evaluate the opposing arguments from Muhammad and other schools.

Core Idea
A second marriage may or may not reset the divorce count; the Hanafi majority extends the muhallil's effect to one and two divorces by analogy.

This lesson explores a classic fiqh dispute: if a man divorces his wife once or twice, she marries another, consummates, and returns to him, does he regain the right to three new divorces? The Hanafi school is split, with Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf arguing for a reset by analogy with the case of three divorces, while Muhammad al-Shaybani and other schools restrict the effect to the severe prohibition. We will examine the proofs and the practical consequences of this disagreement.

Guided Path
1
State the Scenario
Identify the factual scenario: a man divorces his wife one or two times, she remarries, consummates, and then returns to the first husband. The question is whether his right to divorce is restored fully or whether previous divorces count.
This scenario is distinct from the well-known case of three divorces.
2
Identify the Two Positions
Distinguish the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) that the second marriage resets the count, giving the first husband three new divorces, from the opposing position (Muhammad, Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) that it does not reset.
The intra-Hanafi difference is between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.
3
Analyze the Hanafi Proof
The Hanafi proof relies on the hadith term 'muhallil' (one who makes permissible) and qiyas: if the second husband makes the wife permissible after three divorces (strong prohibition), then a fortiori he should do so for less severe cases.
The key is the generality of the term muhallil and the logic of a fortiori argument (qiyas al-awla).
4
Analyze the Opposing Proof and Response
The opposing proof cites that the Qur'an and Sunnah only mention the second husband's effect for three divorces. The refutation in the text argues that the second husband's intercourse is only a condition for the original permissibility, not the cause, and thus its effect is limited to severe prohibition.
The passage does not offer a direct Hanafi rebuttal but directs readers to usul texts.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: under Abu Hanifa, the first husband can divorce three more times; under Muhammad, only one more divorce remains, and a third would make her permanently unlawful without another marriage.
This affects the number of divorces available to the husband and the status of the wife.

Source Text

And an explanation of the disagreement with its proofs: if a man divorces his wife once or twice, and she marries another husband after her 'iddah, then he dies or divorces her after intercourse, then the first husband marries her after the 'iddah, does a new ownership become established for him as in the case of three, or is what has passed counted? According to Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa: the second husband, just as he destroys three and his intercourse establishes a new state of being permissible for the first, such that he possesses three, likewise he destroys what is less than that as well, and establishes a new permissibility. According to Muhammad, al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad, he does not destroy; so if in the second instance he divorces once after he had previously divorced twice, she becomes finally separated (ba'in mughallazah), not lawful for him until she marries another husband; because the Book and the Sunnah ruled that the intercourse of the second husband is a destroyer of the prohibition established by three, not of the light prohibition. And his (Abu Hanifa's) proof: the Prophet named the second husband the 'muhallil' (one who makes lawful), and the muhallil is one who establishes permissibility. Since his intercourse establishes new permissibility in the case of three despite the strength of the prohibition there, it is even more appropriate that he should establish new permissibility for what is less than that despite the lightness of the prohibition. And it is refuted: that the intercourse of the second husband does not in reality establish new permissibility; rather, the establishment of new permissibility is by reference to the original, and his intercourse is a condition for its establishment; hence he is called muhallil. This condition only shows its effect in the severe prohibition, and it does not necessitate that it be a condition in the light prohibition as well; how so? For permissibility remains from some aspect there. And if you wish further detail, refer to the commentaries on 'Usul al-Bazdawi' and the commentaries on 'al-Tahrir'.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of a legal dispute concerning whether a second marriage after a divorce (when the number of divorces is less than three) resets the count, giving the first husband new marital authority to exercise three divorces afresh. The author first states the scenario: a man divorces his wife once or twice, she completes her iddah, marries another man, and then after either death or divorce from the second husband, the first husband remarries her. The question is whether the first husband's right to divorce is restored to the full three (as if the previous divorces never happened) or whether the previous divorces count toward the maximum of three. The author presents the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: just as a second marriage after three divorces destroys the prohibition and establishes a new permission (so the first husband can remarry with full rights), it likewise destroys the effect of one or two divorces. Their proof is analogical: if it works for the stronger case (three), it should work for the weaker a fortiori. They also cite the term 'muhallil' applied by the Prophet to the second husband, which implies making permissible generally. The opposing position (Muhammad, al-Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad) is that the second marriage only destroys the severe prohibition (from three divorces), not the light prohibition (one or two). Their textual proof: the Qur'an and Sunnah only mention the second husband's effect in the context of three divorces. The Hanafi response refutes the opponent's argument by clarifying that the second husband's intercourse does not itself create new permission but is a condition for the permission that originates from the original marriage contract. The condition's effect is only apparent in the severe case, but it does not logically extend to the light case because the light case already retains some permissibility. The author concludes by directing the reader to works of usul for further detail.

Key Terms
مُحَلِّل (muhallil): The second husband who, by consummating the marriage, makes the first wife permissible for her previous husband after a final divorce.
بائنة مغلّظة (ba'in mughallazah): A final irrevocable divorce that occurs after three divorces or after a combination making the woman unlawful without an intervening marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Only al-Shafi'i and Malik
D) Abu Hanifa and Muhammad

Key Takeaway
The effect of a second marriage on the count of divorces is disputed: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf reset the count; Muhammad and other schools do not.

Minimum Period for a Woman to Be Halal After Second Marriage and Trusting Her Statement
States the minimum iddah period and ruling on trusting her statement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum iddah period according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (39 days) and explain why the husband may accept the wife's statement without witnesses.

Core Idea
The minimum iddah is 39 days (two purities + three menses) and the husband may accept her statement without witnesses.

This passage tackles two practical questions: what is the shortest possible iddah after a second marriage? And can the husband rely on his wife's word that she has completed it? It presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the duration (30 vs 39 days) and clarifies the permissibility of accepting her statement based on the nature of marriage as a transaction or religious matter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a woman claiming she has become permissible (halal) to her first husband after a second marriage. The ruling is that if the time frame is plausible and the man strongly believes her, he may remarry her without witnesses.
This is a ruling on the acceptability of a woman's testimony regarding her own iddah.
2
Note the two views on minimum period
Abu Hanifa says one month (30 days) if she affirms the passage of the aqra' (iddah periods). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say 39 days.
The difference arises from how they calculate the minimum iddah.
3
Understand the calculation for 39 days
The 39 days consist of two purity periods (tuhr) of at least 15 days each (30 days) plus three menstrual periods of at least 3 days each (9 days), totaling 39 days.
This is based on the assumption that the divorce occurred in a state of purity and that the minimum menstruation is 3 days and minimum purity is 15 days.
4
Understand why her statement is accepted
Marriage is considered either a transaction (mu'amalah) or a religious matter, and in such matters the statement of one trustworthy person is accepted. Therefore, two witnesses are not required.
The condition is that the time frame must be plausible and the man must have a strong presumption of her truthfulness.
5
Distinguish between the two Hanafi views
Abu Hanifa takes a more lenient view (30 days) based on a different calculation; the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) are more strict (39 days). The passage does not give preference, leaving both as possible positions.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf with practical implications for the husband's reliance on her word.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمبائنة بثلاث لو قالت : حلّلت في مدة تحتمله، وغلب على ظنه صدقها فأخذ المشايخ من الفقهاء بقول شبّان الصحابة له ، وشبان الفقهاء بقول مشايخ الصحابة ، والترجيح بالوجه». انتهى. حلت للأول) : قيل : أقل تلك المدة تسعة وثلاثون يوماً لا بد من ثلاث حيض وطهرين، فأقل مدة الحيض ثلاثة أيام، وأقل الطُّهر خمسة عشر يوماً. قوله : حلت للأول ؛ أي يجوز له أن يعتمد على قولها وينكحها ؛ لأنّ النكاح معاملة أو أمر ديني، وقول الواحد مقبولُ في مثل هذا الباب، فلا يحتاج إلى أن يشهد شاهدان على ذلك. قال في «الكفاية»: «أو في هذه المدة عند أبي حنيفة له شهر إن أقرت بمضي الإقراء، وعندهما: تسعة وثلاثون يوماً، كأنه طلقها في الطهر، وحيضها ثلاثة، وطهرها خمسة عشر يوماً ، فيمضي عدتها بطهرين ثلاثين يوماً، وثلاثة أقراء تسعة أيام». انتهى.
And the one separated by three: if she says, 'I have become permissible [to you]' within a period that could accommodate [the iddah], and he is predominantly confident of her truthfulness, then the elder jurists (mashayikh) among the fuqaha took the statement of the young Companions for him, and the young jurists took the statement of the elder Companions, and the preponderance is by the aspect. End. (The phrase) 'She has become permissible to the first [husband]' – it is said: the minimum of that period is thirty-nine days, necessarily consisting of three menses and two purity periods, because the minimum duration of menstruation is three days, and the minimum purity is fifteen days. His statement: 'She has become permissible to the first' means it is permissible for him to rely on her statement and marry her, because marriage is either a transaction or a religious matter, and the statement of one person is accepted in such a chapter, so there is no need for two witnesses to testify to that. He said in al-Kifayah: 'Or in this period, according to Abu Hanifa, he has a month if she affirms the passage of the iddah periods (aqra'), while according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is thirty-nine days, as if he divorced her in a state of purity, and her menstruation is three, and her purity period fifteen days, so her iddah passes with two purities: thirty days, and three menstrual cycles: nine days.' End.

Commentary
This passage addresses two issues: the minimum period that must elapse for a woman to be considered halal (permissible) for her first husband after a second marriage, and whether the husband may rely on her statement that she is halal. The author begins by citing a view from the masha'ikh (elder jurists) that if the woman says 'I have become permissible' within a time frame that could accommodate the iddah (waiting period), and the man has a strong presumption of her truthfulness, then he may accept her word. This ruling is based on a practice among the Companions: some young Companions accepted the woman's word, while elder Companions required more caution; the preferred view is to accept it. The commentary then defines the minimum period: it is thirty-nine days, calculated as three menstrual periods and two purity intervals, assuming the minimum menstruation is three days and the minimum purity between menses is fifteen days. The text from al-Kifayah clarifies the ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa says the period is one month (thirty days) if she affirms the passing of the iddah by menstruation (aqra'), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it is thirty-nine days. The rationale for the latter is that the iddah is calculated as two purities (30 days) plus three menstrual cycles (9 days) total 39 days. The passage then states the ruling on trusting her: it is permissible (ja'iz) for the man to rely on her word and marry her without two witnesses because marriage is either a transaction or a religious matter, and in such matters the testimony of one person is accepted (qawl al-wahid maqbul).

Key Terms
إقراء (aqra'): The menstrual purity periods (tuhr) or menstrual cycles; in this context, the plural refers to the waiting periods of a woman's iddah.
عدة (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of her husband before she can remarry.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Minimum Period for Woman to Be Halal After Divorce
Explains the minimum period for a woman to become permissible for the first husband after a second marriage, with an intra-Hanafi dispute on the calculation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum 'iddah period after a second marriage according to Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and explain the arithmetic calculation underlying the Sahibayn's view.

Core Idea
The minimum 'iddah is either one month or 39 days, depending on whether the wife's cycles are measured by months or by minimal durations.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about how quickly a woman may remarry her first husband after her second marriage ends. The disagreement turns on whether the 'iddah is determined by the woman's acknowledgment of completed cycles or by a fixed arithmetic minimum. Understanding both views clarifies how Hanafi jurists balance practicality and precaution in family law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal question
The woman becomes halal for the first husband after completing her 'iddah from the second marriage. The dispute is about the minimum possible duration of that 'iddah.
The agreed ruling is that the 'iddah consists of three menstrual cycles (qur') with two purity intervals (tuhr) in between.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that if the woman acknowledges the passing of her cycles, the period is one month. He takes the month as a practical measure, relying on her word.
This view is based on the assumption that three cycles typically occur within a month.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad calculate the minimum as 39 days: three menstruations (3×3=9 days) and two purity periods (2×15=30 days).
This is a precautionary minimum using the shortest possible durations.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, a woman who says her 'iddah ended in 35 days could be believed; under the Sahibayn, she must wait the full 39 days regardless of her claim.
The source does not indicate which view is mufta bihi, so both remain valid within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حلت للأول) : قيل : أقل تلك المدة تسعة وثلاثون يوماً لا بد من ثلاث حيض وطهرين، فأقل مدة الحيض ثلاثة أيام، وأقل الطُّهر خمسة عشر يوماً. 11 ] قوله : حلت للأول ؛ أي يجوز له أن يعتمد على قولها وينكحها ؛ لأنّ النكاح معاملة أو أمر ديني، وقول الواحد مقبولُ في مثل هذا الباب، فلا يحتاج إلى أن يشهد شاهدان على ذلك.
[٢]قوله : قيل ... الخ ؛ قال في «الكفاية»: «أو في هذه المدة عند أبي حنيفة له شهر إن أقرت بمضي الإقراء، وعندهما: تسعة وثلاثون يوماً، كأنه طلقها في الطهر، وحيضها ثلاثة، وطهرها خمسة عشر يوماً ، فيمضي عدتها بطهرين ثلاثين يوماً، وثلاثة أقراء تسعة أيام». انتهى.
حجاب
"She becomes permissible for the first [husband]." It is said: The minimum of that period is thirty-nine days; three menstruations and two purity periods are necessary. So the minimum duration of menstruation is three days, and the minimum purity period is fifteen days. [Commentator] says: "She becomes permissible for the first [husband]" means it is permissible for him to rely on her statement and marry her, because marriage is a transaction or a religious matter, and the word of a single person is accepted in such matters, so there is no need for two witnesses to testify to that. [Another commentator] says: "It is said..." and so on; in al-Kifayah it is said: "According to Abu Hanifa, in this period he has one month if she acknowledges the passing of the cycles. According to the two [companions], [it is] thirty-nine days, as if he divorced her in her purity period, and her menstruation is three days, and her purity period is fifteen days. So her 'iddah passes with two purity periods: thirty days, and three cycles: nine days." End. [Margin: Hijab?]
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the minimum period after which a woman becomes permissible for her first husband (the first husband who divorced her and she then married another man and was divorced by him). The base ruling is that she must complete her 'iddah from the second marriage. The dispute is about the minimum duration of that 'iddah. According to Abu Hanifa, if the woman acknowledges that she has completed her cycles (aقراء), the period is one month. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), the minimum is thirty-nine days. This is calculated based on the minimum menstruation (three days) and minimum purity (fifteen days). The 'iddah requires two purity periods (each a minimum of fifteen days, totaling thirty days) and three menstruations (each a minimum of three days, totaling nine days), summing to thirty-nine days. The passage also clarifies that the first husband can rely on the woman's claim without witnesses because marriage matters are based on trust, not like prescribed punishments.

Key Terms
قرء (qar'): In this text, قرء (plural أقراء) means menstruation (حيض), as used in the calculation of the 'iddah.
طهر (tuhr): The period of purity between two menstruations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, what is the minimum period for a woman to become halal for the first husband after the end of the second marriage?
A) One month
B) Thirty-nine days
C) Forty days
D) Three months

Key Takeaway
The minimum period for a woman to become permissible for her first husband after a second marriage is disputed: Abu Hanifa says one month, the Sahibayn say thirty-nine days, based on different methods of calculating the 'iddah.

Definition and Conditions of Ila' (Vow of Abstinence)
Defines Ila' and sets its minimum duration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Ila' linguistically and legally, and state the minimum duration conditions for free and slave women.

Core Idea
Ila' is an oath to abstain from intercourse for at least four months (free) or two months (slave).

In this lesson, we examine the precise definition of Ila' (vow of abstinence) as established by the Hanafi school. Understanding its linguistic and legal meaning, along with the critical condition of minimum duration, is essential to distinguish it from regular oaths and to grasp its legal consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic definition
Recognize that 'Ila'' linguistically means an oath in general. This sets the foundation for the legal definition.
Linguistically, it is simply 'oath' (hulf).
2
Identify the legal definition
Understand that legally, Ila' is an oath to abstain from sexual intercourse with one's wife, confirmed by a binding oath, for a minimum period.
The oath must be difficult to break (e.g., by Allah) to indicate genuine prevention.
3
State the condition of minimum duration
Note that the duration must be at least four months for a free woman and two months for a slave woman. If shorter, it is not Ila'.
There is no maximum limit.
4
Distinguish Ila' from non-Ila' oaths
Recognize that if a husband abstains without an oath or for a shorter period, it is a regular oath, not Ila'.
Breaking a regular oath only requires kaffarah; Ila' has additional consequences after the period.
5
Explain the rationale for halving for slaves
Understand that the reduction to half for a slave woman is due to the general principle of slavery affecting rulings, similar to divorce and 'iddah.
This principle is consistent across various family law rulings.

Chapter of Ila'. (And it is an oath that prevents intercourse with the wife (13) its duration): i.e., the duration of Ila'. (So there is no Ila' if he swears for less than it, and it is for the free woman four months, and for the slave woman two months.) [1] He says: "Chapter of Ila'" – linguistically it is an oath absolutely; one says: aala yooli ilaan if he swears. In sacred law, it is an expression for preventing oneself from approaching the married woman for four months or more, a prevention confirmed by an oath. Thus in al-'Inayah (3). [2] He says: "an oath" – for if he abandons intercourse for four months or more due to laziness or anger without an oath, it is not legally Ila'. The oath includes swearing by Allah and the conditional [forms] mentioned previously, and it is restricted to that which is difficult [to fulfill] to indicate prevention. So if he says: "If I have intercourse with you, then for Allah upon me is that I pray two rak'ahs," it is not Ila'. Thus in al-Fath. [3] He says: "the wife" – present or future, so it includes suspended Ila', like his saying to a non-relative woman: "If I marry you, then by Allah I will not approach you," and it requires the same conditions as suspending divorce, i.e., it must be added to ownership. (4) He says: "its duration" is an adverb for "prevents." [0] He says: "So there is no Ila'" i.e., legally, and the summary is that if he swears not to have intercourse with her for two months or one month, it is not legal Ila', and its subsequent ruling does not apply. Rather, its ruling is that if he does not have intercourse during that period, nothing is upon him; and if he has intercourse during it, he must expiate for the oath, as in other oaths. [6] He says: "and it is" – this is a clarification of the minimum duration; there is no limit for its maximum. The reason for the difference between the duration for a free woman and that for a slave woman is that slavery has an effect of halving; thus his divorce of her is two [revocable divorces], and her 'iddah is two menstruations, and other such rulings. (1) Even if [the oath] concerns property, like his saying to a non-relative woman: "If I marry you, by Allah I will not approach you," because the consideration is at the time of actualization of Ila'. See Radd al-Muhtar (2:545). (2) al-'Inayah (4:188).
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on Ila' (vow of abstinence). It begins with a definition: Ila' is an oath that prevents the husband from having intercourse with his wife. The key condition is the minimum duration: for a free woman, it is four months; for a slave woman, it is two months. If a man swears to abstain for less than that, it is not considered Ila' legally; instead, it is a regular oath. If he breaks it by having intercourse, he must pay kaffarah (expiation). The commentary clarifies that Ila' must be by a binding oath (e.g., swearing by Allah or conditional forms that imply a pledge). If a man simply abandons intercourse without an oath, it is not Ila'. The wife can be either current or future (e.g., if he says to a non-relative: 'If I marry you, I will not approach you'). The duration is halved for slave women due to the general principle that slavery reduces rulings by half, similar to divorce and 'iddah. The passage also notes that there is no maximum limit for Ila' – the husband can swear for longer than the minimum.

Key Terms
إيلاء (ila'): In the sacred law, it is an oath to abstain from sexual intercourse with one's wife for a period of four months or more (for a free woman).
حلف (hulf): An oath, specifically in the context of Ila', it must be an oath that is difficult to break (e.g., by Allah) and indicates prevention of intercourse.
الحرّة (al-hurrah): A free woman; her Ila' duration is four months.
الأمة (al-amah): A slave woman; her Ila' duration is two months.

Ila' is defined by an oath to abstain from intercourse for at least four months (free) or two months (slave); failing this condition means it is a regular oath, not Ila'.

Definition and Ruling of Ila' (Vow of Abstinence)
Defines ila' and states its rulings with Quranic proof and Sahaba dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition and conditions of Ila' and explain the Hanafi position on automatic divorce after four months, including the Sahaba dispute.

Core Idea
After four months of abstinence without return, a divorcing divorce occurs automatically — that is the Hanafi reading of the Quranic resolve.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah defines Ila' and lays out its essential conditions. It also presents the Quranic proof for the ruling and the famous dispute among the Companions about whether divorce occurs automatically or requires further action. Understanding this will help you see how the Hanafi school derives its position from the text and weighs different Sahaba opinions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition and essential conditions of Ila'
Read the opening definition: Ila' is a vow that prevents intercourse for a minimum duration (4 months free, 2 months slave), and must be an oath that causes hardship. List the conditions from the text.
Conditions include: oath, minimum duration, burden, wife (present or future).
2
Locate the Quranic dalil and understand its interpretation
The verse from Surah al-Baqarah (2:226-227) is cited. Notice how the Hanafi school interprets 'resolve on divorce' as the mere passage of four months without return.
The phrase 'wa in 'azamu al-talaq' is key.
3
State the Hanafi position on the effect of four months passing
The Hanafi ruling: after four months without fi', one divorcing divorce (ba'in) occurs automatically, based on reports from Ibn Abbas, Ali, and Ibn Mas'ud.
4
Identify the opposing view (Ibn Umar) and their reasoning
Ibn Umar and others held that divorce does not occur automatically; rather, the husband is made to wait after four months until he decides to return or divorce.
Another view (Imran) says it is a revocable divorce.
5
Understand the tarjih mechanism and the thamarah al-khilaf
The Hanafi school adopts the view of the majority of Sahaba as stronger. The practical difference: under Hanafi, the wife is divorced after four months; under Ibn Umar's view, she remains married.
This is the mufta bihi position.

[٣] قوله : مؤيّد ; أي ليس فيه تقييد بأربعة أشهر، والحاصل أنه إذا حلف على ترك الوطء مقيداً بأربعة أشهر فصاعداً أو مؤبداً بذكر قوله: «أبداً»، ونحوه، أو مطلقاً، أيضاً مؤبد حكماً ، فإن وطئ في أثناء أربعة أشهر من وقتِ الحلف يسقط الإيلاء وتجب كفارة اليمين. وإن لم يطأ حتى مضت أربعة أشهر وقعت عليه طلقة واحدة بائنة، بخلاف ما إذا حلف على أقل من أربعة أشهر ، فإنّه لا وقوع للطلاق هناك، بل إن بر فذاك، وإن حنث فعليه كفارة يمين. [؟]
Chapter of Ila' (vow of abstinence) 
A vow that prevents intercourse with the wife for its duration, so there is no ila' if he vowed for less than that duration, and it (the minimum duration) is four months for a free woman and two months for a slave woman.
[1] His statement: 'Chapter of Ila''; Ila' linguistically means absolute oath; it is said: aala yuli ilaan if he swore. In Sacred Law: it is an expression of restraining oneself from approaching the married woman for four months or more, a restraint emphasized by an oath. This is from al-'Inayah. [2] His statement: 'a vow'; if he left intercourse for four months or more out of laziness or anger without a vow, it is not Ila' legally. The vow includes swearing by Allah and conditional statements as previously mentioned, and it is restricted to what causes hardship to indicate prevention; if he said: 'If I have intercourse with you, I must pray two rak'ahs for Allah', it is not Ila'. This is from al-Fath. [3] His statement: 'the wife' (including present or future) includes suspended Ila', such as saying to a non-mahram woman: 'If I marry you, by Allah I will not approach you.' The conditions are the same as those for suspending divorce regarding its being added to ownership. [4] His statement: 'its duration' is an adverb for 'prevents'. [5] His statement: 'so there is no Ila'; i.e., legally, and its summary: if he vows not to have intercourse with her for two months or one month, it is not legal Ila', and its subsequent ruling does not apply; rather, if he does not have intercourse during that period, nothing is upon him, and if he does have intercourse, he must expiate the oath, as in other oaths. [6] His statement: 'and it (the minimum duration)' explains the minimum duration; there is no maximum. The reason for the difference between the duration for free women and that for slave women is that slavery has an effect of halving, which is why her divorce is two, her waiting period two menstrual cycles, etc.
[PAGE_374]
Its ruling: one divorcing divorce if he fulfills, and expiation and penalty if he breaks it. If he says: 'By Allah, I will not approach you' or 'I will not approach you for four months', the first is permanent, the second is limited to four months.
[1] His statement: 'Its ruling'; the basis of this chapter is His statement: {For those who swear off their wives is a waiting period of four months. If they return, then Allah is Forgiving, Merciful. And if they resolve on divorce, then Allah is Hearing, Knowing.} The meaning of 'if they return' is that they return during the period by intercourse, and when unable due to illness or similar, by saying 'I have returned' or similar. The meaning of 'if they resolve on divorce' is by the passing of four months without intercourse. Thus reported from Ibn 'Abbas, 'Ali, and Ibn Mas'ud, as recorded by al-Bayhaqi, Ibn Abi Hatim, Ibn al-Mundhir, 'Abd ibn Humayd, and others. Regarding this issue there is a disagreement among the Companions: from Ibn 'Umar and others: 'Divorce does not occur merely by the passage of four months; rather, he is made to wait after that until he holds or divorces.' From 'Imran: 'The end of four months is a revocable divorce.' I have expanded on this topic in al-Ta'liq al-Mumajjad on Muwatta' Muhammad.
[2] His statement: 'if he breaks it'; i.e., by intercourse during this period, then expiation of the oath becomes obligatory if he swore by Allah, and the penalty is incurred if he attached something, like freeing a slave or similar.
[3] His statement: 'permanent'; i.e., it does not have a restriction of four months. The summary: if he vows to leave intercourse restricted to four months or more, or permanently by mentioning 'forever' or similar, or absolutely, it is also permanent by legal effect. If he has intercourse during the four months from the time of the vow, the Ila' drops and expiation of the oath is obligatory. If he does not have intercourse until four months have passed, one divorcing divorce occurs upon him, unlike if he vowed for less than four months, for then divorce does not occur there; rather, if he fulfills, fine, and if he breaks it, he owes expiation of the oath. [?]
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains the chapter of Ila' (vow of abstinence) from the Hanafi madhhab. It begins by defining Ila' as an oath that prevents marital intercourse for a specific minimum duration: four months for a free woman and two months for a slave woman, due to the effect of slavery halving the duration. The author emphasizes that Ila' requires an oath; mere avoidance without an oath does not constitute Ila'. The vow must be inherently difficult to fulfill to indicate prevention; if the penalty is light, it is not true Ila'. The wife includes those who will become wives, so a suspended Ila' before marriage is valid. If the oath is for less than the minimum duration, it is not legal Ila' and only requires expiation if broken. The passage then quotes the Quranic verse from Surah al-Baqarah (2:226-227) as the primary proof. The author explains that 'return' means resuming intercourse during the period, and 'resolve on divorce' means the passage of four months without intercourse, which results in a divorcing divorce according to the Hanafi school. This is based on the understanding of Ibn 'Abbas, 'Ali, and Ibn Mas'ud. However, there is a Sahaba dispute: Ibn 'Umar held that divorce does not occur automatically; instead, the husband is made to wait after four months. 'Imran reported that the passage of four months results in a revocable divorce. The Hanafi position adopts the view of the majority of Sahaba, even though the author does not explicitly justify the tarjih here. The ruling also notes that if the husband breaks his vow during the four months, he must expiate his oath (if by Allah) or fulfill the attached penalty (e.g., freeing a slave). At the end of the four months, if he has not resumed intercourse, a divorcing divorce takes effect. This is for vows of four months or more; vows of less than four months carry no divorce even after the period passes, only expiation if broken.

Key Terms
الإيلاء (al-ila'): A vow to abstain from marital intercourse for four months or more, emphasized by an oath.
الفيء (al-fay'): Returning to marital intercourse during the period of Ila', or verbal declaration if unable.
الحنث (al-hinth): Breaking the vow by having intercourse during the Ila' period, which triggers expiation (kaffarah) and penalty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if a husband makes a valid Ila' (vow to abstain for four months) and does not have intercourse with his wife during those four months?
A) The marriage continues and he must expiate his oath.
B) One divorcing divorce (ba'in) occurs automatically after four months.
C) The wife can immediately seek a judicial divorce.
D) The husband is made to wait indefinitely until he decides to return or divorce.

Key Takeaway
Ila' is a binding vow of abstinence for four months (free) or two months (slave); if no return occurs, a divorcing divorce takes effect automatically according to the Hanafi school.
