Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Ruling of Ila' (Vow of Abstinence) and Its Quranic Proof
States ruling, cites Quran, and discusses companion ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling of Ila' and explain the Quranic proof, including the interpretation of the Companions that supports the Hanafi position.

Core Idea
Ila' leads to automatic ba'in divorce after four months without intercourse — the Hanafi position based on Quran 2:226-227 and Ibn Abbas' interpretation.

This lesson introduces the fiqh of Ila' — a husband's vow to abstain from marital intercourse. The central ruling is that after a waiting period of four months without intimacy, one ba'in divorce automatically takes effect. We will examine the Quranic proof from Surah al-Baqarah and the different interpretations among the Companions that shaped the Hanafi school's position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is Ila'? The passage states the ruling: one ba'in divorce if the husband fulfills (i.e., does not break the oath by returning within four months), and expiation/penalty if he breaks it. Note the two cases: permanent (indefinite) and temporary (four months).
The ruling distinguishes between the consequence of non-intercourse (divorce) and breaking the oath (expiation).
2
Locate the dalil
The Quranic verse cited: Surah al-Baqarah 2:226-227. Identify that the verse mandates a waiting period of four months and mentions 'return' (faa') and 'resolve on divorce' (azamu al-talaq).
The verse is the primary textual evidence for Ila'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the verse prove automatic divorce? The Hanafis, following Ibn Abbas, Ali, and Ibn Mas'ud, interpret 'resolve on divorce' as the lapse of four months without intercourse. The imperative 'tarbus' indicates obligation of waiting; the silence on further action means divorce is effective immediately upon expiration.
The interpretative step is key: 'cazamu' is understood as the passage of time, not a new intention.
4
Note the companion ikhtilaf
Ibn Umar and others held that divorce does not occur automatically; the husband should be stopped and given a choice. 'Imran considered it a revocable divorce. The Hanafi school adopts the view of Ibn Abbas et al.
The ikhtilaf affects the practical outcome: automatic vs. requiring additional action.
5
Distinguish between vows of four months or more and less than four months
If the vow is for less than four months, no divorce occurs after the period expires; the only consequence is expiation if the oath is broken. If the vow is for four months or more, failure to return within four months triggers automatic ba'in divorce.
This distinction is critical for applying the ruling correctly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحكمه : طلقة بائنة إن برّ، والكفارة والجزاء إن حنث. فلو قال : والله لا أقربك ، أو لا أقربك أربعة أشهر : الأوَّلُ مؤبد، والثاني مؤقت بأربعة أشهر. [١] قوله : وحكمه؛ الأصل في هذا الباب قوله تعالى: {لِلَّذِينَ يُؤْلُونَ مِن نِّسَابِهِمْ تَرَبُّصُ أَرْبَعَةِ أَشْهُرٍ فَإِن فَاءُ و فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ غَفُورٌ رَّحِيمٌ} {وَإِنْ عَزَمُوا الطَّلَقَ فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ سَمِيعٌ عَلِيمٌ}، ومعنى قوله : فإن فاء : رجعوا في المدة بالوطء، وعند العجز عنه بسبب مرض ونحوه بقوله : فئت ونحوه. ومعنى وَإِنْ عَزَمُوا الطَّلَقَ : أي بانقضاء أربعة أشهر بدون وطء، هكذا روي عن ابن عباس وعلي وابن مسعود عند البيهقي وابن أبي حاتم وابن المنذر وعبد بن حميد وغيرهم، وفي المسألة خلاف للصحابة : فعن ابن عمر وغيره : إنّه لا يقعُ الطلاقُ بمجرد مضي أربعة أشهر، بل يوقف بعده حتى يمسك أو يطلق، وعن عمران : انقضاء الأربعة طلاق رجعي، وقد بسطت الكلام في هذا المقام في التعليق الممجّد على موطأ محمد. [٢] قوله : إن حنث ؛ أي بالوطء في هذه المدّة فتجبُ كفّارة اليمين إن حلف بالله ، وترتب الجزاء إن عَلقَ به شيئاً ، كعتق العبد ونحوه. [٣] قوله : مؤيّد ؛ أي ليس فيه تقييد بأربعة أشهر، والحاصل أنه إذا حلف على ترك الوطء مقيداً بأربعة أشهر فصاعداً أو مؤبداً بذكر قوله: «أبداً»، ونحوه، أو مطلقاً، أيضاً مؤبد حكماً ، فإن وطئ في أثناء أربعة أشهر من وقتِ الحلف يسقط الإيلاء وتجب كفارة اليمين. وهو وإن لم يطأ حتى مضت أربعة أشهر وقعت عليه طلقة واحدة بائنة ، بخلاف ما إذا حلف على أقل من أربعة أشهر ، فإنّه لا وقوع للطلاق هناك، بل إن بر فذاك، وإن
And its ruling: one ba'in divorce if he fulfills, and expiation and penalty if he breaks the oath. So if he said: 'By Allah, I will not approach you,' or 'I will not approach you for four months' – the first is permanent, the second is temporary for four months. [1] He said: 'And its ruling'; the basis of this chapter is His statement: {For those who swear off their wives, a waiting period of four months; if they return, then indeed Allah is Forgiving, Merciful} {And if they resolve on divorce, then indeed Allah is Hearing, Knowing}. And the meaning of His statement 'if they return' is that they return during the period by intercourse; and in case of inability due to illness etc., by saying 'I have returned' etc. And the meaning of 'and if they resolve on divorce' is by the lapse of four months without intercourse. Thus it is narrated from Ibn Abbas, Ali, and Ibn Mas'ud... and there is a difference of opinion among the Companions: from Ibn Umar and others that divorce does not occur merely by the lapse of four months, but he is stopped thereafter until he either holds her back or divorces; and from 'Imran that the lapse of four months is a revocable divorce... [2] He said: 'if he breaks his oath' i.e., by intercourse during this period, so the expiation of the oath becomes obligatory if he swore by Allah, and the penalty is incurred if he attached something to it, like freeing a slave etc. [3] He said: 'permanent' i.e., it has no restriction to four months. The summary: if he swore to abandon intercourse restricted to four months or more, or permanently by saying 'forever' etc., or absolutely, it is also effectively permanent. If he has intercourse during the four months from the time of the oath, the Ila' falls and the expiation of the oath becomes obligatory. And if he does not have intercourse until four months have passed, one ba'in divorce occurs upon him. Unlike if he swore for less than four months, then no divorce occurs there; rather, if he fulfills then that is it, and if
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage opens with the ruling of Ila' (a vow to abstain from intercourse with one's wife). The author states that the ruling is: if the husband fulfills his vow (i.e., returns to marital relations within the period), he incurs no divorce but must pay expiation if he swore by Allah; if he breaks the vow by approaching his wife, expiation is due. The base text then gives two examples: an absolute vow (unrestricted) and a vow limited to four months. The first is permanent (i.e., the vow is unbounded) and the second is temporary (restricted to four months). The commentary begins by citing the Quranic basis from Surah al-Baqarah (2:226-227). The term 'faa' (return) is explained as sexual intercourse, or in case of illness, a verbal declaration. 'Resolving on divorce' means the passage of four months without intercourse. This interpretation is attributed to Ibn Abbas, Ali, and Ibn Mas'ud, and is reported by several hadith sources. A difference among the Companions is noted: Ibn Umar holds that divorce does not occur automatically after four months; rather, the husband is given a choice to reconcile or divorce. According to 'Imran, the lapse of four months constitutes a revocable divorce. The Hanafi school adopts the view of Ibn Abbas et al., as will be clarified. The next segment explains 'breaking the oath': if the husband has intercourse during the four-month period, he must pay the expiation for an oath (if he swore by Allah) or fulfill the attached condition (such as freeing a slave). The term 'permanent' is then defined: a vow not restricted to four months, whether explicitly permanent or absolute (unrestricted), is considered effectively permanent. If intercourse occurs within four months, the Ila' is lifted and expiation is due. If no intercourse occurs until four months pass, one ba'in divorce takes effect. This is contrasted with a vow for less than four months: in that case, no divorce occurs at all regardless of passage of time; the only consequence is expiation if the oath is broken. The page ends mid-sentence, continuing to the next lesson.

Key Terms
إيلاء (ila'): A vow or oath taken by a husband to abstain from sexual intercourse with his wife for a specified period or indefinitely.
برّ (birr): Fulfilling the oath by returning to intercourse within the period? Actually, in this context, 'birr' means the husband fulfills his vow by not breaking it (i.e., he does not have intercourse during the period, thus the vow is kept). However, the passage states: 'إن برّ' meaning if he fulfills, i.e., he does not break the oath, which in the context of Ila' means he does not return to intercourse within the period? Wait, careful: The ruling says: 'طلاق بائن إن برّ' — if he fulfills (i.e., keeps the vow by not having intercourse), he gets a ba'in divorce? That seems inconsistent because if he fulfills (by abstaining), why divorce? Actually, the meaning is: if he fulfills his oath (i.e., he does not break it by having intercourse), then after four months, a ba'in divorce occurs. But if he breaks it (by having intercourse), he pays expiation. So 'birr' here refers to the completion of the waiting period without breaking the oath.
حنث (hanth): Breaking the oath by having intercourse with the wife during the period of Ila'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) No divorce occurs; the husband must pay expiation.
B) One ba'in divorce occurs automatically after four months.
C) The marriage continues, but the husband must go to court.
D) A revocable divorce occurs.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that Ila' results in automatic ba'in divorce after four months without intercourse, based on Quran 2:226-227 and the interpretation of key Companions.
